+ Scp: Unmarked Doors Archive — Score: 64.5
Prompt:
Write an SCP entry about a series of identical unmarked doors appearing in abandoned buildings worldwide that lead to a massive, architecturally impossible archive. Documents within reference a previous global civilization destroyed by an unspecified containment failure. Foundation researchers discover references to their own organization under a different name, including personnel files for current staff dated centuries ago. Include exploration logs revealing sections of the archive actively being removed by entities resembling hazmat teams who flee when approached, and evidence that O5 Council members have visited the archive without authorization. Third person (exploration team perspective) with recovered document excerpts. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
SCP-XXXX: "The Echo Archive" Object Class: Euclid Special Containment Procedures: All instances of SCP-XXXX are to be monitored and secured by Foundation personnel. Access to SCP-XXXX is restricted to Level 3 personnel and above, with prior approval from at least two Level 4 personnel. Any attempts by entities resembling hazmat teams to remove documents or materials from SCP-XXXX are to be intercepted and detained for questioning. Description: SCP-XXXX refers to a series of identical unmarked doors that have appeared in abandoned buildings worldwide. These doors, measuring approximately 2 meters in height and 1 meter in width, are made of a material resembling stainless steel and feature a doorknob with a distinctive scratch pattern. The doors are always found in areas with limited access and are not visible on any known maps or blueprints. When opened, each door leads to a massive, architecturally impossible archive (hereafter referred to as "The Archive"). The Archive appears to be a vast, labyrinthine repository of documents, files, and artifacts, with shelves stretching indefinitely in all directions. The interior of The Archive is dimly lit, with a faint hum of machinery audible in the distance. Exploration of The Archive has revealed a vast array of documents, including texts, images, and audio recordings, detailing the history and culture of a previously unknown global civilization. This civilization, referred to as "The Precursors," appears to have been destroyed by an unspecified containment failure. Notably, documents within The Archive contain references to an organization known as "The Guardians of the Veil," which bears striking similarities to the Foundation. Personnel files for current Foundation staff have been discovered, dated centuries ago. These files contain accurate biographical information, including dates of birth and death, as well as detailed psychological profiles. **Recovered Document Excerpts:** * " Incident Report: Breach of Containment Facility-7. The failure of our primary containment protocols has resulted in the catastrophic destabilization of our global ecosystem. The consequences of this event will be irreparable. Recommendations for future containment procedures are appended." (Dated 1756) * "Personnel File: Dr. Maria Rodriguez. Date of Birth: 1985. Date of Death: 2053. Psychological Profile: Highly intelligent and resourceful, with a tendency towards obsessive behavior. Recommended for Level 3 clearance and assignment to anomalous artifact research." (Dated 1821) * "Memo: Reorganization of The Guardians of the Veil. Following the Incident of '45, it has been deemed necessary to restructure our organization to prioritize containment and research over exploration and discovery. All personnel are expected to adapt to these new protocols." (Dated 1845) Exploration Log XXXX-1: On//20, a team of Level 2 researchers, accompanied by two Level 3 security personnel, entered SCP-XXXX-4 (located in an abandoned warehouse in). The team navigated the Archive for approximately 30 minutes before encountering a group of entities resembling hazmat teams, who were actively removing documents from the shelves. The entities, numbering approximately six, were dressed in full hazmat suits and carried large duffel bags. When approached, the entities fled, leaving behind several documents and a small, handheld scanner. Analysis of the scanner revealed a proprietary encryption protocol, which has been decrypted and is currently under study. Exploration Log XXXX-2: On//20, a team of Level 3 researchers, accompanied by two Level 4 security personnel, entered SCP-XXXX-7 (located in an abandoned library in). The team discovered a section of the Archive that appeared to have been recently removed, with shelves torn from the walls and debris scattered throughout the area. A search of the surrounding area revealed a hidden logbook, belonging to an individual identified as "O5-█". The logbook detailed several unauthorized visits to SCP-XXXX, including meetings with entities resembling the hazmat teams encountered during Exploration Log XXXX-1. **Addendum XXXX-1:** Following the discovery of the logbook, O5-█ has been placed under administrative review. Further investigation into the activities of O5 Council members is ongoing. **Addendum XXXX-2:** Analysis of the proprietary encryption protocol has revealed a possible connection to a previously unknown anomalous entity, designated as SCP-XXXX-1. Further research is required to determine the nature and purpose of this entity. In light of these discoveries, SCP-XXXX has been reclassified as Euclid. Further exploration and research are necessary to fully understand the nature and purpose of The Archive, as well as the implications of the documents and artifacts contained within.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This SCP entry demonstrates a solid understanding of the SCP Foundation format and successfully incorporates most of the requested elements. The piece follows the standard SCP documentation structure with object class, containment procedures, description, and exploration logs. The concept of doors leading to an impossible archive containing records of a previous civilization is compelling and fits well within SCP lore. The writing maintains an appropriately clinical, bureaucratic tone throughout, which is essential for SCP entries. The author successfully includes the key plot elements: identical doors in abandoned buildings, an architecturally impossible archive, references to a destroyed civilization, personnel files for current staff dated centuries ago, hazmat-like entities removing documents, and evidence of unauthorized O5 visits. However, the execution has several notable weaknesses. The recovered document excerpts feel somewhat generic and lack the unsettling specificity that makes the best SCP entries memorable. The dates and details don't create a cohesive timeline or deeper mystery. The exploration logs are functional but lack atmospheric detail that would make the archive feel truly alien or threatening. The piece suffers from some tell-don't-show issues, particularly in describing the archive's impossibility and the entities' behavior. More sensory details and specific observations would enhance the reader's immersion. The writing is competent but lacks the subtle horror and existential dread that elevates exceptional SCP entries. The structure is sound but predictable, following a very standard SCP format without creative flourishes. While this isn't necessarily a flaw, it makes the piece feel somewhat routine. The implications of the discovery - that the Foundation may be cyclical or that reality itself may be unstable - are present but not fully explored or made viscerally unsettling. The piece meets the technical requirements and word count while maintaining internal consistency, but it doesn't transcend its functional nature to become truly engaging or memorable. + Classic sci-fi: Offworlder (Le Guin) — Score: 53.0
Prompt:
Classic sci-fi: Offworlder (Author style: Le Guin) Write a chapter following a young diplomatic envoy sent to address tensions on a distant human colony where humanity has diverged into distinct subspecies through both natural adaptation and separation of lineages. Against protocol, the envoy slips away from official functions to walk the streets alone, encountering markets, ordinary citizens, and social structures that contradict the official briefings. Upon returning to their quarters, the envoy is reprimanded by Command, and is tasked with approaching the stationed Minister of Science (a political posting rather than scientific). A challenging conversation ensues, in which the envoy's wits and will are tested, by a seasoned political operator looking to test the mettle of the offworlder. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
Chapter 3: Unofficial Observations I slipped away from the ceremonial procession, shedding my escort of starched officials and protocol officers. The bright sunlight and dusty air of Newhaven's capital city, Kyrios, enveloped me like a warm shroud. I breathed deeply, feeling the weight of diplomatic duty lifting from my shoulders. For a few precious hours, I was just another face in the crowd. As I walked, the city's vibrant markets unfolded before me. Merchants touted their wares – exotic spices, hand-woven textiles, and peculiar, glowing artifacts – in a cacophony of languages. I marveled at the diversity of humanity on display. Here, the descendants of Earth's diaspora had adapted to their environment in ways both subtle and profound. The Kyr'zhik, with their iridescent skin and angular features, haggled over prices with the sturdy, compact Sorensi. Meanwhile, the tall, slender Valtorians watched from the shadows, their eyes gleaming with an unnerving intensity. I wandered, taking in the intricate stone architecture that seemed to blend seamlessly into the natural landscape. Carved glyphs adorned the buildings, referencing old Earth myths: the labors of Hercules, the exploits of Gilgamesh, and the whispers of the Oracle of Delphi. These symbols spoke to a shared heritage, a connection to the distant past that bridged the gaps between these divergent human subspecies. As I explored, I encountered ordinary citizens going about their daily lives. A group of children, their faces a kaleidoscope of skin tones and features, chased each other through the market stalls, laughing and playing. An elderly couple, their eyes clouded with age, sat on a bench, watching the world go by with a deep contentment. These were the people I had come to serve, not the politicians and officials who had greeted me with such formality. My reverie was shattered by the insistent chime of my comms device. I reluctantly made my way back to the diplomatic quarters, knowing I would face reprimand for my unauthorized excursion. Upon entering my quarters, I was greeted by the stern face of Commandant Ortega, projected from the comms screen. "Envoy, you have compromised protocol. Your actions will be noted in your report." I stood at attention, trying to appear contrite. "I apologize, Commandant. I needed to...clear my head." Ortega's expression softened slightly. "I understand the pressure, Envoy. However, your duties require a certain...decorum. You have a meeting with Minister of Science, Elwes, scheduled for this afternoon. I suggest you prepare accordingly." I nodded, though my mind was already racing with the implications of this meeting. Minister Elwes was a political appointee, not a scientist. This conversation would be a test of my diplomatic skills, a probing of my mettle by a seasoned operator. As I entered the Minister's office, I was struck by the opulent decor. The walls were adorned with holographic displays, showcasing the wonders of Newhaven's unique ecosystem. Elwes, a tall, imposing figure with a charming smile, rose from behind his desk. "Envoy, welcome. I trust you're finding our...humble city to your liking?" I took a seat, trying to gauge the Minister's intentions. "It's a remarkable place, Minister. The diversity of human experience here is...fascinating." Elwes leaned back in his chair, steepling his fingers. "Yes, we've developed a certain...flavor, here on Newhaven. But I'm sure you're aware of the tensions simmering beneath the surface. The Kyr'zhik and Sorensi have...differences, shall we say. And the Valtorians...well, they're a special case, aren't they?" I sensed a trap, a subtle probing of my allegiances. "I'm here to listen, Minister. To understand the complexities of this situation and find a path forward that benefits all parties." Elwes chuckled, a low, throaty sound. "Ah, Envoy, you're a true diplomat. But let me tell you, the game here is not about finding common ground. It's about navigating the currents of power, of influence. And I'm afraid you're not yet...buoyant enough to ride these waves." I met his gaze, refusing to back down. "I'm willing to learn, Minister. But I must emphasize that my role is to facilitate cooperation, not to further entrench divisions." Elwes leaned forward, his eyes glinting with a challenge. "We'll see about that, Envoy. We'll see about that." The conversation had barely begun, and already I felt like a sailor navigating treacherous waters. I steeled myself for the battles ahead, knowing that the fate of Newhaven's fragile peace hung in the balance.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to capture Le Guin's style but falls short in several key areas. The writing demonstrates a basic understanding of the prompt requirements - featuring a diplomatic envoy exploring a colony with divergent human subspecies, an unauthorized walkabout, and a confrontation with a political figure. However, the execution lacks the sophisticated subtlety and philosophical depth characteristic of Le Guin's work. The worldbuilding shows promise with the three subspecies (Kyr'zhik, Sorensi, Valtorians) and their physical adaptations, but the descriptions feel superficial and somewhat generic. The cultural details like the carved glyphs referencing Earth mythology are interesting but underdeveloped. The market scene, while attempting to show diversity, relies on familiar tropes without the nuanced social observation Le Guin would provide. The protagonist's voice lacks the introspective quality and moral complexity typical of Le Guin's characters. The first-person narration feels more like a standard adventure story than the thoughtful, anthropological perspective Le Guin would employ. The character's motivations for the unauthorized excursion are weakly established - "clear my head" is insufficient justification for a diplomatic breach. The ending feels abrupt and doesn't deliver on the promised "challenging conversation" - it's more of a brief verbal sparring match that establishes conflict without exploring it meaningfully. The prose occasionally veers toward purple territory with phrases like "enveloped me like a warm shroud" and "kaleidoscope of skin tones," but generally maintains readability. However, it lacks the elegant precision and philosophical weight that defines Le Guin's style. + Biopunk: Polymerase Chain Reaction — Score: 57.0
Prompt:
Biopunk -- Polymerase Chain Reaction Write a chapter set in a near-future post-apocalyptic world where corporate genetic engineering was designed with built-in obsolescence—engineered DNA lasting only one generation to maximize profits before societal collapse. Follow a biohacker working with salvaged equipment to splice viable food crops for their settlement using rapidly degrading genetic material. As world building / window dressing, include details about jury-rigged lab equipment, and the physical toll (and unexpected upsides) of using untested genetic modifications as medicine. The plot of this chapter is centred around a black market contract. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**Chapter 7: Splicing Hope** The air reeked of ozone and burnt plastic as I hunched over the makeshift lab bench, eyes fixed on the flickering display of the PCR machine. The solar panel rig outside, cobbled together from scavenged parts, struggled to provide a stable voltage, threatening to fry the delicate equipment at any moment. I muttered a silent prayer to the DIY gods, willing the machine to hold together just a little longer. My name is Lena, and I'm a biohacker – a genetic engineer in a world where the corporations that once ruled the planet had designed their creations with built-in obsolescence. They'd engineered DNA to last only one generation, ensuring a constant stream of profits before the inevitable collapse of society. Now, in the aftermath, those of us who'd managed to survive were left to pick up the pieces and try to rebuild. My settlement, New Eden, was one of the lucky ones. We'd managed to scrounge up a few functional labs, and I'd spent years learning to work with the salvaged equipment. My specialty was splicing viable food crops from the rapidly degrading genetic material left behind by the corporations. It was a never-ending battle, as the DNA itself seemed to be unraveling before our eyes. I worked with a pair of gloves, the synthetic skin worn thin in places, as I carefully pipetted a sample of the latest batch of genetic material into the PCR machine. The display flickered, and I held my breath as the machine whirred to life. This was the part where I usually crossed my fingers and hoped for the best. The contract had come in through the black market, a whispered rumor of a buyer willing to pay top dollar for a custom splice. The client wanted a crop that could thrive in the toxic soil of the old industrial zones – a tall order, but one that could mean the difference between life and death for our settlement. I'd agreed to take on the job, despite the risks. As I worked, my mind wandered to the physical toll of using untested genetic modifications as medicine. I'd seen it firsthand – the mutations, the unpredictable side effects, the occasional catastrophic failure. But what choice did we have? The corporations had taken their research and development with them when they abandoned the planet. We were left to improvise, to jury-rig solutions from scraps. I'd tried some of the mods myself, of course. The painkillers I'd engineered from a combination of opium poppy and venomous snake DNA had been a game-changer for our settlement's medical team. But there were downsides – the vivid dreams, the occasional bout of paranoia. I'd learned to live with it, but I knew others who hadn't been so lucky. The PCR machine beeped, signaling the end of the cycle. I carefully extracted the sample and began the process of sequencing the DNA. The results would take a few hours to process, but I had a good feeling about this one. As I worked, I thought about the client, wondering who they were and what their true motives were. The black market was a treacherous place, full of opportunists and charlatans. But the pay was too good to pass up, and I'd taken precautions – a dead drop, a secure comms channel, the whole nine yards. The hours ticked by, the sun dipping below the horizon as I worked. The lab grew darker, the only light coming from the flickering display of the PCR machine and the soft glow of the solar panel rig. I'd almost forgotten about the contract when the comms device on my wrist beeped, signaling an incoming message. I raised my arm, and a holographic display flickered to life above my wrist. The message was encrypted, but I recognized the digital signature – it was the client. "Lena, this is Phoenix. I've received your proposal. I'm willing to meet your price, but I need to see results. Can you deliver?" I hesitated, weighing the risks. But the prospect of that payday was too enticing to resist. "I can deliver," I typed back, my fingers flying across the virtual keyboard. "But I need more time. The sequencing is still running." There was a pause, and for a moment, I wondered if I'd overplayed my hand. "Very well," the response came. "You have 48 hours. If I don't see results, the deal is off." I nodded, even though I knew the client couldn't see me. "Understood. I'll have something for you soon." The comms device went dark, and I let out a slow breath. I had 48 hours to create a miracle. Time to get to work.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This biopunk chapter demonstrates solid adherence to the prompt's requirements, establishing a post-apocalyptic world where corporate genetic engineering included planned obsolescence. The author successfully incorporates the requested elements: a biohacker protagonist working with salvaged equipment, degrading genetic material, jury-rigged lab equipment, and a black market contract as the central plot device. The worldbuilding is competent, with details like the solar panel rig threatening to fry equipment and the PCR machine cobbled together from scavenged parts. The concept of DNA designed to last only one generation is well-integrated into the narrative. The physical toll of genetic modifications is addressed through Lena's experience with her engineered painkillers, showing both benefits (effective pain relief) and drawbacks (vivid dreams, paranoia). However, the execution suffers from several technical and stylistic issues. The prose tends toward tell-don't-show, particularly in exposition-heavy passages explaining the world's backstory and Lena's situation. Phrases like "My name is Lena, and I'm a biohacker" feel clunky and overly direct. The writing occasionally becomes overwrought with unnecessary dramatic flourishes like "prayer to the DIY gods." Character development is minimal. Lena functions more as a vehicle for exposition than a fully realized person. Her motivations are straightforward (survival, money) but lack emotional complexity. The mysterious client "Phoenix" remains a cipher, which while appropriate for the black market setting, doesn't add tension or intrigue. The dialogue, limited to the encrypted message exchange, feels functional but lacks personality or distinctive voice. The pacing is uneven, with long stretches of technical description followed by brief action sequences. The chapter's structure follows a predictable pattern: setup, work montage, client contact, deadline pressure. While this serves the story adequately, it doesn't offer surprising developments or creative plot turns. The ending feels somewhat abrupt, more like a pause than a proper chapter conclusion. Technical aspects like sentence flow are generally adequate, though some constructions feel awkward. The tone remains consistent throughout, maintaining the gritty, resourceful atmosphere appropriate to the setting. + Classic sci-fi: The Azra Gambit — Score: 64.3
Prompt:
Classic sci-fi (Author style: Asimov) The Azra Gambit Colonial mars is being mined by corporations who take leases on indentured labourers. The thing they are mining is Azra, a recently discovered exotic metal which accelerates radioactive decay to such a rate that it is greatly sought after for interstellar drives and weapons alike. This has created both a gold rush and an arms race as various interests vie for control and endeavour to unlock Azra's secrets. The story follows Arthur Neegan, a first generation settler and mining engineer. Upon discovering that his unassuming plot sits atop an immense Azra vein, he is subjected to a flurry of interest and scrutiny. Write the next chapter in this story, in which an armed retinue descends on Arthur's home and politely but forcefully invites him to a meeting with some unknown party off-world. The insignia look like that of the Antares diplomatic corp -- diplomatic in name only. Arthur finds himself in the centre of a political tug of war. The chapter involves a meeting with this unknown party, who makes Arthur an offer. The scene should be primarily dialogue, interspersed with vivid description & scene setting. It should sow hints of the larger intrigue, stakes & dangers. Include Asimov's trademark big-and-small-picture world building and retrofuturistic classic scifi vibe. The chapter begins with Arthur aboard the transfer vessel, wondering just what he's gotten involved in. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
Chapter 3: The Antares Envoys Arthur Neegan fidgeted with the stiff collar of his formal attire, a far cry from the practical jumpsuits he was accustomed to wearing on the Martian mining sites. The transfer vessel, emblazoned with the Antares diplomatic corp's insignia, hurtled through the void, its gentle hum a reminder of the vast distances being traversed. The armed retinue that had escorted him to the vessel had been courteous, yet firm, in their insistence that he attend this meeting. Arthur's curiosity was piqued, but his unease was growing by the minute. As the vessel docked at a nondescript space station, Arthur was greeted by a tall, imposing figure in a tailored black suit. The man's eyes seemed to bore into Arthur's very soul, yet his smile was warm and disarming. "Mr. Neegan, welcome. I am Ambassador Zhou, representing the Antares diplomatic corp. Please, follow me." Arthur trailed behind the ambassador, his eyes drinking in the opulent decor of the space station's reception area. The walls were adorned with intricate, swirling patterns that seemed to shift and shimmer in the light, a testament to the advanced technology at play. They arrived at a spacious conference room, where a lone figure awaited. The individual, a woman with piercing green eyes and raven-black hair, rose from her seat as Arthur entered. Her attire was a stark contrast to the ambassador's, a flowing white gown that seemed to defy gravity. "Mr. Neegan, this is Director Elara Vex of the Antares Research Initiative," Ambassador Zhou announced, his voice low and smooth. Director Vex extended a slender hand, her smile a calculated blend of warmth and authority. "Ah, Mr. Neegan, it's an pleasure to finally meet you. Please, join us." As Arthur took his seat, he couldn't help but notice the subtle, yet unmistakable, emblem on Director Vex's lapel – the stylized, curved blade of the Antares Research Initiative. Rumors whispered that this organization was the true power behind the diplomatic corp's façade, pulling the strings from the shadows. "Mr. Neegan," Director Vex began, her voice like honey, "we've been following your... exploits on Mars. Your discovery of the Azra vein has sent shockwaves throughout the industry. We believe your unique expertise would be invaluable in unlocking the secrets of this remarkable metal." Arthur's instincts screamed caution, but he played along, intrigued by the prospect of collaborating with the enigmatic Director Vex. "I'm flattered, Director. However, I'm just a mining engineer. What makes you think I'm the right person for this task?" Director Vex leaned forward, her eyes glinting with intensity. "We've analyzed your work, Mr. Neegan. Your innovative approaches to Azra extraction and processing have not gone unnoticed. We believe your... unorthodox methods could be the key to harnessing Azra's true potential." Ambassador Zhou chimed in, his voice a soothing counterpoint to Director Vex's intensity. "We're willing to offer you a substantial package, Mr. Neegan – a significant share of the profits, access to our cutting-edge research facilities, and, of course, a guarantee of your safety and security." Arthur's mind reeled as he processed the offer. The promise of wealth and prestige was enticing, but the whispered rumors of the Antares Research Initiative's true nature and the director's unnerving gaze made him hesitant. "I appreciate the offer, Director," Arthur said, choosing his words carefully, "but I need to know more about what I'd be getting myself into. What exactly do you hope to achieve with Azra, and what's the nature of this... research initiative?" Director Vex's smile never wavered, but a flicker of something – annoyance, perhaps, or calculation – danced in her eyes. "Let's just say, Mr. Neegan, that our goals are aligned with the greater good of humanity. We aim to unlock Azra's secrets, to harness its power for the betterment of our civilization. As for the initiative... let's simply say that we're a coalition of like-minded individuals and organizations, working together to advance human knowledge and progress." Arthur sensed the carefully crafted words, the subtle evasions, and the unspoken implications. He was being drawn into a web of intrigue, where the stakes were higher than he could have ever imagined. "I see," Arthur said, stalling for time, his mind racing with the implications. "I'll need to consider your offer, Director. May I ask, what's the timeframe for this... collaboration?" Director Vex's gaze seemed to bore into his very soul. "Time, Mr. Neegan, is a luxury we don't have. The Azra gold rush is intensifying by the day, and we need your expertise to stay ahead of the curve. We require your decision within the next 48 hours. After that... let's just say that the window of opportunity will have closed." As the meeting drew to a close, Arthur couldn't shake the feeling that he was standing at the edge of a precipice, staring into an abyss of unknown dangers and unspoken consequences. The Antares diplomatic corp's true intentions, the nature of the research initiative, and the secrets hidden within the swirling patterns on the space station's walls all swirled together in a maddening dance, leaving him wondering what he had truly gotten himself into.
Judge Evaluation:

+ Contemporary romance: Darkroom Revelations — Score: 50.7
Prompt:
Darkroom Revelations Write a first-person narrative from the perspective of Dani, a 25-year-old assertive art student known for her bold style and take-charge attitude in relationships. For the past semester, she's been quietly fascinated by Elliot (he/him), a 19-year-old boy in her experimental photography class. Dani has been intrigued by his unconventional masculinity: killer thrift-shop-nu-goth style, soft demeanour and quiet intellect. When they're paired for a final project requiring late nights in the darkroom, Elliot tentatively shares that he's been questioning his gender identity and expression. Set during one of these intimate darkroom sessions where the red light creates a confessional atmosphere. Explore Dani's complex attraction—her usual assertiveness complicated by her desire to protect Elliot's vulnerability, her excitement at witnessing his self-discovery, and her confusion about what this means for her own identity as someone typically attracted to more defined gender presentations. The narrative should capture the tender awkwardness of their conversations, Dani's internal struggle between taking charge and wanting to give Elliot agency, and the unexpected chemistry that develops as both find themselves in uncharted territory. 1000 words.
Model Output:
I adjusted the safelight, the dim red glow illuminating the darkroom like a warm hug. Elliot and I had been paired for our final project, and I was determined to make it count. Our experimental photography class had been a highlight of my semester, and I was excited to see what we could create together. As we worked, the silence between us was comfortable, punctuated only by the occasional clink of chemicals or the soft whir of the enlarger. I couldn't help but steal glances at Elliot, his nu-goth style a fascinating contrast to his soft demeanor. His thrift-store finds were always impeccably curated, and I loved the way he paired black fishnets with tartan shirts. It was like he was daring the world to question his aesthetic, and I admired that about him. But it was more than just his style that drew me in – it was the quiet confidence he exuded, the way he seemed to own his space without ever being loud or boisterous. As we worked, Elliot began to open up to me in ways I hadn't expected. At first, it was just small talk – favorite photographers, music, and movies. But as the nights wore on, our conversations deepened. He shared with me his love of poetry, his passion for social justice, and his struggles with anxiety. I found myself drawn to his vulnerability, my usual assertiveness tempered by a desire to protect him from the world. It wasn't until we were well into our project, surrounded by the musty smell of developer and the soft glow of the safelight, that Elliot shared something that made my heart skip a beat. "I've been thinking a lot about my gender identity," he said, his voice barely above a whisper. "I don't know if I'm a boy, or if I'm something else entirely." My mind went blank. I had suspected that Elliot might be queer, but I hadn't expected this. I didn't know how to respond, my usual confidence deserting me. But as I looked at Elliot, I saw the vulnerability in his eyes, the fear of rejection and uncertainty. I knew I had to be careful, to give him the space he needed to explore his identity. "Hey, that's okay," I said, trying to sound calm. "You don't have to have all the answers right now. Just being open to exploring your identity takes a lot of courage." Elliot smiled, a small, tentative smile. "Thanks, Dani. Just talking about it makes me feel a little better." As we continued to work, our conversations became more intimate, more personal. I found myself drawn to Elliot's quiet strength, his willingness to question everything and challenge the status quo. I was excited to witness his self-discovery, to see him grow and evolve as a person. But as I watched him, I couldn't help but feel a twinge of confusion. I had always been attracted to people with more defined gender presentations – confident, assertive, and unapologetic. Elliot's vulnerability and uncertainty threw me off balance, making me question my own identity and what I wanted in a partner. As the night wore on, our chemistry became harder to ignore. We would brush arms, our skin touching as we worked, and I would feel a spark of electricity run through my body. I didn't know what to do with these feelings, or how to reconcile them with my desire to protect Elliot's vulnerability. At one point, as we were printing a particularly tricky negative, Elliot turned to me and our eyes met. For a moment, we just stared at each other, the tension between us palpable. I felt like I was drowning in his gaze, like I was being pulled under by a riptide of emotion. I looked away, my heart racing. I didn't know what to do, or how to process these feelings. But as I glanced back at Elliot, I saw that he was smiling at me, a soft, gentle smile. "Hey," he said, his voice barely above a whisper. "I think we make a pretty good team, don't you?" I nodded, my throat dry. "Yeah," I said, my voice barely above a whisper. "I think we do." As we finished up our project, the darkroom seemed to shrink around us, the air thick with tension. I knew that I had to be careful, to give Elliot the space he needed to explore his identity. But I also knew that I couldn't ignore the chemistry between us, the spark of attraction that had ignited in the dim red glow of the safelight. As we left the darkroom, the cool night air hitting us like a slap in the face, I realized that I was in uncharted territory. I didn't know what the future held, or how our relationship would evolve. But I did know one thing – I was excited to find out.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This narrative attempts to tackle a complex and sensitive subject matter involving gender identity exploration within an intimate creative setting. The piece demonstrates some strengths in establishing atmosphere and character dynamics, but suffers from several significant weaknesses that undermine its overall effectiveness. The darkroom setting is well-utilized as both a literal and metaphorical space for intimate revelation, with the red light creating an appropriately confessional atmosphere. The author successfully establishes the basic character dynamics between Dani and Elliot, capturing some of the awkwardness inherent in their situation. However, the narrative suffers from substantial issues with character development and emotional authenticity. Dani's voice lacks the assertiveness and boldness described in the prompt - she comes across as generically supportive rather than displaying the complex internal struggle between her natural take-charge attitude and her desire to give Elliot agency. Her attraction and confusion about her own identity preferences are mentioned but never deeply explored or made visceral for the reader. The dialogue feels stilted and unnatural, particularly during the crucial gender identity revelation scene. Elliot's confession feels abrupt and disconnected from the preceding conversation, while Dani's response is disappointingly generic and therapeutic rather than reflecting her specific personality and internal conflict. The piece relies heavily on telling rather than showing, particularly regarding the characters' emotions and the development of chemistry between them. Phrases like "our chemistry became harder to ignore" and "the tension between us palpable" substitute for actual demonstration of these dynamics through action, dialogue, or specific behavioral details. The writing contains several amateurish elements, including repetitive phrasing ("barely above a whisper" appears multiple times), vague emotional descriptions, and a tendency toward melodramatic moments that feel unearned. The ending's optimistic tone doesn't feel sufficiently grounded in the character work that preceded it. While the piece attempts to address complex themes around gender identity and attraction, it does so in a surface-level way that doesn't fully engage with the psychological and emotional complexity the prompt demanded. + Contemporary romance / drama: Stolen Moments in Roma — Score: 44.8
Prompt:
Contemporary Romance / Drama: Stolen Moments in Roma. Write a series of interconnected short scenes and dialogues that span a single day in modern-day Rome, in narrative form. This will form the beginning of a larger story. Alessandra, a fiery, independent Roman woman who works as a motorcycle courier, nearly collides with Ben, a somewhat clumsy, overly polite British academic on sabbatical, who is engrossed in a guidebook near the Trevi Fountain. The initial encounter is a clash of cultures and personalities – Alessandra is all sharp wit and rapid-fire Italian, while Ben is flustered apologies and awkward attempts at speaking the language. However, as they sort out the near-miss, a spark of unexpected humor and connection emerges. Alessandra, it quickly becomes clear, is a whirlwind of energy and mischief. She's a self-admitted troublemaker with a secret penchant for kleptomania, a detail she doesn't explicitly reveal, but which manifests in subtle, daring acts throughout the day. She impulsively decides to take Ben on a wild, unsanctioned tour of Rome, dragging him in some specific instances far outside his comfort zone. Ben, despite his initial apprehension and inherent politeness, finds himself utterly captivated by Alessandra's unapologetic spirit and zest for life. He is drawn into her orbit, a willing participant in increasingly outlandish situations, a quiet rebellion brewing beneath his scholarly exterior. The narrative should primarily consist of short, vivid scenes and dialogue exchanges, revealing their contrasting personalities and backgrounds, and the growing, ambiguous tension between them. Ben is captivated by Alessandra's energy and the thrill of breaking free from his routine. There's a clear sense that Alessandra is toying with Ben, pushing his boundaries and enjoying his reactions, but her own feelings remain somewhat enigmatic. The day should be a rollercoaster of exhilarating, slightly dangerous, and humorous moments, leaving Ben completely disoriented but utterly smitten. Explore the underlying tension & chemistry between them, culminating in some payoff as they part ways (or not -- your choice). Include this detail: Write in narrative prose, using immersive storytelling. 1000 words.
Model Output:
The sun beat down on the cobblestone streets of Rome, casting a warm glow over the bustling crowds. Alessandra zoomed through the throngs on her motorcycle, her dark hair whipping behind her like a banner. She was a force to be reckoned with, a whirlwind of energy and mischief. Her eyes sparkled with a perpetual glint of troublemaking, and her sharp wit could cut down anyone who dared to cross her. As she turned a corner near the Trevi Fountain, she nearly collided with a hapless tourist, his nose buried in a guidebook. Alessandra swerved to avoid him, her tires screeching in protest. "Oh, mio dio!" she exclaimed, leaping off her bike. "Watch where you're going, idiota!" The tourist, a gangly Brit with a look of perpetual apology, stumbled backward, his eyes wide with alarm. "Oh, I'm so sorry! I wasn't watching where I was going. I'm terribly sorry!" Alessandra rolled her eyes, but a hint of amusement danced in her voice. "You're sorry? You're sorry? You're going to get yourself killed, amico! What's wrong with you?" Ben, the tourist, looked like he'd been slapped. "I-I was just trying to find the Trevi Fountain. I got distracted by the map..." Alessandra snorted. "The fountain's right behind you, genius. You can't miss it." She jerked her head toward the Baroque masterpiece. "Now, are you going to stand there all day, or are you going to move?" Ben's face turned bright red as he hastily apologized again, but Alessandra was already striding toward him, her long legs eating up the distance. "Come on, I'll show you the real Rome. Not the tourist traps and overpriced gelato. The real deal." Ben's eyes widened as Alessandra grabbed his arm, propelling him into a wild, unsanctioned tour of the city. They careened through narrow alleys, dodged street performers, and stumbled upon hidden piazzas. Ben's initial apprehension gave way to exhilaration as Alessandra's infectious energy drew him in. At a street market, Alessandra snatched a handful of fresh figs from a vendor's stall, winking at Ben as she popped one into her mouth. "Try one! They're divine." Ben hesitated, but Alessandra's laughter was contagious. He bit into the sweet, jammy fruit, and their eyes met in a spark of shared delight. As they explored, the skies grew dark, and a sudden downpour drenched the city. Alessandra spotted a gelato shop and yanked Ben under the awning, laughing. "Buonissimo! Gelato and a storm – the perfect combination." Inside, the shop was cozy, the scent of waffle cones and hazelnut wafting through the air. Ben watched, mesmerized, as Alessandra charmed the shop owner into giving them free samples. Her Italian was a rapid-fire staccato, punctuated by expressive gestures and sparkling eyes. As they licked their gelato, Ben felt the tension between them build. Alessandra's proximity was like a live wire, sparking and crackling with energy. He couldn't help but be drawn to her unapologetic spirit, her zest for life. Their fingers touched as they reached for the same flavor, and a jolt of electricity ran through Ben's body. Alessandra's eyes met his, a mischievous glint dancing in their depths. The storm outside intensified, drumming against the awning like a primal heartbeat. Ben felt himself becoming lost in the whirlwind that was Alessandra, his senses overwhelmed by the sights, sounds, and sensations of the day. As the rain slowed to a drizzle, Alessandra pulled him back into the streets, the city transformed by the storm's passage. Water pooled on the cobblestones, reflecting the vibrant colors of the buildings. They walked in silence, the only sound the squelching of their shoes on the wet pavement. Ben felt a sense of disorientation, as if he'd been turned upside down and shaken. As they reached the edge of the piazza, Alessandra turned to him, her eyes sparkling with mischief. "Grazie, amico. Today was... illuminating." Ben's heart skipped a beat. "I think I need a map to navigate you, Alessandra." Her laughter was a throaty, husky sound, sending shivers down his spine. "You don't need a map, Ben. You just need to keep up." With that, she turned and disappeared into the crowd, leaving Ben staring after her, utterly smitten and completely disoriented. The city seemed to spin around him, a kaleidoscope of colors and sounds, but his eyes remained fixed on the spot where Alessandra had vanished. As he stood there, a small, enigmatic smile playing on his lips, Ben knew that his life was about to become very, very interesting.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to capture a whirlwind romance in Rome but suffers from several significant weaknesses that undermine its effectiveness. The story follows the basic premise adequately - a near-collision between Alessandra, a motorcycle courier, and Ben, a British academic - but fails to deliver on many of the specific requirements and lacks narrative sophistication. The characterization is superficial and relies heavily on stereotypes. Alessandra is presented as a "fiery Italian" with "sharp wit" but her dialogue doesn't demonstrate genuine wit - it's mostly aggressive and one-dimensional. Ben is the bumbling, overly apologetic Brit, but his character development feels rushed and unconvincing. The promised kleptomania trait is barely explored, appearing only in a brief fig-stealing scene that lacks the subtlety requested. The dialogue is particularly weak, often feeling stilted and unnatural. Alessandra's speech patterns don't convincingly capture rapid-fire Italian-accented English, and Ben's responses are generic. The conversations lack the spark and chemistry that should drive a romance narrative. The prose suffers from tell-don't-show problems throughout. Rather than demonstrating Alessandra's mischievous nature through actions and dialogue, the narrator simply states she's "a whirlwind of energy and mischief." The writing relies heavily on clichéd descriptions like "eyes sparkled" and "infectious energy." The pacing feels rushed, cramming too many scenes into limited space without allowing moments to breathe or develop naturally. The transition from near-collision to impromptu tour happens too quickly to feel believable. The storm sequence feels particularly forced and convenient. The ending attempts to create romantic tension but feels unearned given the shallow character development. Ben's transformation from cautious academic to "utterly smitten" happens without sufficient justification or gradual build-up. The piece does capture some sense of Roman atmosphere and maintains basic coherence, but it reads more like a rough first draft than polished creative writing. The prose occasionally veers toward purple ("like a live wire, sparking and crackling") without earning its heightened language through emotional depth. + Cozy sci-fi: The Last Outpost — Score: 61.6
Prompt:
Cozy spacepunk The Last Outpost Nettle (or Nets to her friends) bartends at The Last Outpost -- a lazy hub for miners and merchants in an asteroid belt on the Andromeda outer rim. Escaping from her past life, Nets found a home here at the Outpost. They have, thus far, tolerated Net's flaws which she tries to keep in equilibrium with her assortment of talents. Her evenings involve chatting with patrons, negotiating the drama, intrigue, problems & love lives of the diverse crowd that filter through the Outpost. Tonight is no different, at least, until a frazzled looking stranger, tentacled dreads askew, quietly plops down at the bar: "Vega whisky, neat. Better make that a double." Write a chapter in this story. Establish conflict for narrative interest. Don't resolve the conflict within this chapter. Aim for about 60% dialogue. First person, present tense. 1000 words.
Model Output:
I wipe down the bar with a dirty rag, surveying the familiar faces of the evening crowd. Miners fresh off a long haul, their coveralls stained with asteroid dust, swap stories of close calls and lucky strikes. Merchants haggle over cargo and trade routes, their eyes locked on the holographic displays projected above the bar. The usual suspects, all with their own dramas and intrigues. I know them all by name, and they know me as Nets, the bartender with a talent for listening and a penchant for getting into trouble. Just as I'm pouring a round of drinks for a rowdy group of asteroid prospectors, the door to the Outpost slides open and a stranger walks in. He's a sight to behold – tentacled dreads, askew and frazzled, like he's been through a war. His eyes scan the room, locking onto the bar before he makes a beeline for me. "Vega whisky, neat," he says, his voice low and rough. "Better make that a double." I raise an eyebrow as I grab the bottle of Vega's finest. "Tough day?" I ask, pouring a generous double shot into a glass. He takes the drink from me, his long fingers wrapping around the glass like a vice. "You have no idea." I lean against the bar, intrigued. "Try me." He takes a sip of the whisky, his eyes closing in appreciation. "I've been running for...I don't know, feels like an eternity. Just trying to get my head down and catch my breath." I nod sympathetically. "Well, you're safe here. The Outpost's a bit of a haven, even if it doesn't look like much." He opens one eye, regarding me warily. "What's the catch?" I smile. "No catch. Just...lively conversation, occasionally interrupted by explosions or fistfights." He raises an eyebrow. "Exploding fistfights?" I chuckle. "Okay, maybe that's a bit of an exaggeration. But we do get our fair share of excitement around here." Just then, a loud shout goes up from the corner of the room, followed by the sound of shattering glass. I sigh, pushing off from the bar. "Excuse me, I think I'm needed over there." As I make my way through the crowd, the stranger's voice follows me. "Nettle, right? I'm...Kael." I turn back, flashing him a quick smile. "Nets, to my friends. Nice to meet you, Kael." By the time I've mediated the dispute – a minor squabble between two rival mining crews – and restored order to the Outpost, Kael has finished his drink and is nursing a second. I take a moment to study him, trying to get a read on this mysterious stranger. He's definitely running from something, or someone. The way he keeps glancing over his shoulder, the tension in his shoulders...it all screams ' trouble'. But there's something about him that draws me in, something that makes me want to know more. As I approach him, a familiar face appears at my elbow – Lyra, our resident tech expert and all-around genius. "Nets, I need to talk to you about something," Lyra says, her voice low and urgent. I raise an eyebrow. "What's up?" Lyra glances at Kael before leaning in close. "I've been monitoring the comms channels, and I think we've got a problem. There's a ship incoming, requesting docking clearance. But the thing is...it's not responding to hails." My gut tightens. "What do you mean?" Lyra's eyes are serious. "I mean, it's not answering our calls. And I've run the ship's ID through the database...it doesn't match anything on file." I feel a shiver run down my spine. This doesn't sound good. Not good at all. "Get the boss," I tell Lyra, already moving to intercept the incoming ship's docking request. "We need to figure out what's going on here." As I make my way to the comms station, I can feel Kael's eyes on me, watching me with an intensity that makes my skin prickle. I get the feeling that this stranger is about to become a whole lot more than just another face in the crowd.

+ Young adult drama: Gone South — Score: 41.2
Prompt:
Young adult drama Gone South Taylor is a 16 year old teen with a history of "concerning behavioural patterns" (or that's how the stupid smug school counsellor worded it on the phone call to Mom). It shouldn't be a surprise: When you live in a backwater town in Tennessee, your choices are: a. be mind-fuckingly bored, or b. invent some drama. Two days ago, Taylor came out to their family as trans. This disclosure was *not* in the category of invented drama -- it was, in fact, the real deal, and a long time coming. It didn't go well. The last 48 hours had been pure disaster. In a moment of desperate inspiration, Taylor had decided to get the hell out of dodge. And so an escape plan was hatched and executed within the space of 30 minutes. That was last night. Now Taylor was two states away, having been unceremoniously ejected from their hitched ride in downtown New Orleans. Write the next chapter in Taylor's story as they find their feet in this new environment. Tell the chapter over the course of their first day in New Orleans, in which Taylor meets another runaway with issues and secrets. Taylor navigates this new world, not knowing who to trust or what the dangers are. Write in Taylor's voice, and incorporate their internal monologue as they grapple with intense & conflicting emotions. Also incorporate dialogue with the interesting characters Taylor meets. First person, mixed tense. 1000 words.
Model Output:
I stood on the corner of Bourbon and Canal, clutching my backpack and trying to wrap my head around the fact that I was actually here. New Orleans. The city of jazz and voodoo and...well, not exactly the welcoming arms I'd been hoping for. The guy who'd given me a ride had dumped me here, muttering something about needing to get to a meeting. I'd been too stunned to even ask what meeting. As I scanned the crowded street, my phone buzzed in my pocket. Mom. Again. I silenced it, feeling a pang of guilt mixed with a healthy dose of fear. I didn't know what to say to her, or how to face the fallout from my impulsive decision. I'd left without thinking, without a plan, and now I was stuck in a city with no charger, no money, and no idea what I was doing. I took a deep breath, trying to shake off the anxiety that had been building since I'd left home. I had to focus on the present. Find a way to survive, at least for the next few days. I spotted a small café across the street and made a beeline for it. Maybe they'd have a charger, or at least a sympathetic ear. As I pushed open the door, a bell above it rang out, and I was enveloped in the warm scent of coffee and baked goods. Inside, the café was cozy, with mismatched tables and chairs scattered about. A girl with bright pink hair and a nose ring looked up from behind the counter, raising an eyebrow as she took in my disheveled appearance. "Hey, you okay? You look like you've been through a war," she said, her voice dripping with a thick Southern drawl. I hesitated, unsure how much to reveal. But something about her kind eyes put me at ease. "Just a long night," I said, trying to sound casual. "I'm Taylor. I'm...new here." The girl nodded, her expression softening. "I'm Jesse. Welcome to the Big Easy, Taylor. What can I get you?" I hesitated, unsure what I could afford. "Just...water, please?" Jesse raised an eyebrow but said nothing, handing me a glass of ice-cold water. As I took a sip, I noticed a guy sitting in the corner, his eyes fixed on me with an intensity that made my skin prickle. "Who's that?" I asked Jesse, nodding towards the guy. Jesse followed my gaze, her expression wary. "That's Ryder. He's...a regular. Don't mind him, he's just...Ryder." I nodded, taking another sip of my water. Ryder didn't look like someone to be trifled with, but I was too tired to care. As I sat down at the counter, Jesse started to chat with me, asking me about my story. I found myself opening up to her, telling her about my family, about coming out, about the desperation that had driven me to leave. Jesse listened intently, her eyes never leaving mine. When I finished, she nodded thoughtfully. "I get it," she said. "I've been there too, in my own way. I ran away from home when I was 15. Been on my own ever since." I felt a spark of connection with Jesse, a sense of understanding that I hadn't experienced in a long time. As we talked, Ryder got up and approached us, his eyes still fixed on me with an unnerving intensity. "Jesse, who's your new friend?" he asked, his voice low and gravelly. Jesse rolled her eyes. "Ryder, this is Taylor. Taylor, Ryder. Don't mind him, he's just trying to intimidate you." Ryder smirked, his eyes glinting with amusement. "I'm just trying to get to know you, Taylor. You're new around here, right?" I nodded warily, unsure what to make of Ryder's sudden interest. "Yeah, I just got here last night," I said, trying to sound nonchalant. Ryder's eyes narrowed. "What brings you to our fair city?" I hesitated, unsure how much to reveal. But there was something about Ryder that made me feel like he already knew my secrets. "I'm just...exploring," I said finally. Ryder raised an eyebrow. "Exploring, huh? Well, I can show you around, if you want. I know this city like the back of my hand." I exchanged a wary glance with Jesse, who shrugged. "It's up to you, Taylor," she said. "But be careful, okay? Ryder's...got his own way of doing things." I nodded, unsure what to make of Ryder's offer. But as I looked into his eyes, I saw something there that gave me pause. A glimmer of understanding, of recognition. Maybe, just maybe, I'd found someone who got it. Someone who understood what it was like to be a runaway, to be a misfit. As I nodded, accepting Ryder's offer, I felt a spark of hope ignite within me. Maybe this city, this crazy, chaotic place, could be my chance to start anew. To find myself, to find my place in the world. And maybe, just maybe, I'd found someone to share that journey with.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to capture Taylor's vulnerable first day in New Orleans as a trans teen runaway, but suffers from several significant weaknesses that undermine its effectiveness. The writing adheres to most basic instructions - it's written in first person from Taylor's perspective, covers their first day in New Orleans, introduces other runaway characters, and includes internal monologue. However, it fails to deliver the requested "mixed tense" and doesn't reach the 1000-word target, appearing closer to 800 words. The character development is superficial. Taylor comes across as a generic troubled teen rather than a specifically trans character dealing with family rejection. Their voice lacks authenticity and the internal monologue feels perfunctory rather than genuinely conflicted. Jesse and Ryder are introduced as stock characters - the helpful café worker and the mysterious potentially dangerous stranger - without meaningful depth or distinguishing characteristics. The dialogue is particularly weak, relying on exposition and clichéd exchanges. Lines like "Welcome to the Big Easy, Taylor" and "I know this city like the back of my hand" feel stilted and unnatural. The conversations don't reveal character or advance the plot meaningfully. The prose suffers from extensive tell-don't-show problems. Rather than demonstrating Taylor's emotional state through actions and concrete details, the narrative simply states feelings: "feeling a pang of guilt mixed with a healthy dose of fear" and "I felt a spark of connection with Jesse." The writing lacks the sensory details and atmospheric richness that could bring New Orleans to life. The pacing feels rushed and the plot developments are predictable. The ending pivots too quickly toward hope and connection without earning these emotional beats. Taylor's willingness to trust Ryder despite obvious warning signs strains credibility, and the sudden optimism feels incongruent with the established tone of desperation and vulnerability. The piece also lacks the emotional complexity promised by the setup. Taylor's experience as a rejected trans teen should carry more weight and specificity, but instead we get generic runaway angst that could apply to any troubled teenager. + Dystopic-comedy: My Apocalypse Buddy — Score: 51.6
Prompt:
My Apocalypse Buddy Write a wry, dry short story of survival and adventure loosely in the style of Terry Pratchett, set in the post-technological collapse world. The story begins with the pair deliberating their predicament and intent for the day's mission, details the ways in which the mission inevitably goes sideways, and returns them to home base in multiple ways, worse for wear. [characters] - the animo-tronic stuffed koala, Chewy, from some long forgotten before time - midas, our hapless protagonist, who has a knack for finding himself in the worst kinds of trouble. 1000 words.
Model Output:
Midas scratched the grime from his eyes, surveying the ruins of civilization from the relative comfort of their makeshift base. Chewy, the animo-tronic stuffed koala, perched on a nearby crate, its glassy eyes flicking between various shades of blue as it processed their predicament. "Right, Chewy," Midas said, "today's mission: scrounge up some edible food, maybe some decent water. You know, the essentials." Chewy's eyes flashed a brief, skeptical yellow. Midas took it as a sign of approval, or at least, a lack of outright dissent. Their base, a scavenged gas station on the outskirts of the ravaged city, offered a modicum of safety. The pumps were dry, but the building still stood, a testament to the ingenuity of pre-Apocalypse construction. Midas and Chewy had claimed it as their own, decorating the interior with a mishmash of salvaged goods and makeshift repairs. With a deep breath, they set out into the unknown. The sun beat down upon them, casting long shadows across the abandoned streets. Chewy's eyes flickered a concerned orange as Midas navigated the rubble-strewn roads. Their first stop, a nearby grocery store, promised a potential bounty. Midas pushed open the creaking door, and they slipped inside. The air was stale, heavy with the scent of decay. Chewy's eyes dimmed to a faint, worried purple as Midas led the way through the darkened aisles. It wasn't long before they stumbled upon their first obstacle: a rival scavenger, a burly man with a scar above his left eyebrow. He eyed Midas and Chewy with a mixture of curiosity and hostility. "Finders, keepers," the man growled, his hand resting on the grip of a holstered pistol. Midas, ever the diplomat, attempted to reason with the man. Chewy, sensing the tension, flashed a bright, warning red. The situation escalated, with the rival scavenger attempting to relieve Midas of his trusty crowbar. A brief, intense scuffle ensued, ending with Midas and Chewy making a hasty retreat, pursued by the angry scavenger. As they fled, Chewy's eyes pulsed a frantic, electric blue. Midas stumbled, his foot catching on a loose paving stone. They tumbled to the ground, with Chewy bouncing off Midas's chest. The rival scavenger, closing in for the kill, was suddenly distracted by a loud, rumbling noise. A massive, mutant rat, easily the size of a small car, emerged from the nearby sewer. Its beady eyes fixed on the scavenger, who turned to flee. Midas and Chewy took advantage of the chaos, scrambling to safety as the rat gave chase. Breathless and shaken, they stumbled upon a small, abandoned garden. Amidst the overgrown vegetation, they discovered a hidden cache of canned goods and a few precious bottles of water. Midas's eyes lit up with excitement, but Chewy's flickered a cautious, amber warning. As they prepared to leave, the garden's owner, a grizzled old survivalist, emerged from the underbrush. She eyed Midas and Chewy with a mixture of suspicion and curiosity. "You two look like you could use a meal," she said, her voice a low, gravelly growl. "But don't think about getting too comfortable. This ain't no charity." Midas and Chewy exchanged a wary glance. Chewy's eyes pulsed a tentative, greenish-yellow, suggesting they might be in for a surprise. The old survivalist led them to a nearby campfire, where a makeshift stew simmered in a battered pot. As they ate, the old woman regaled them with tales of the pre-Apocalypse world. Chewy's eyes sparkled with a nostalgic, sky blue, while Midas listened intently, his eyes wide with wonder. Their respite was short-lived, however. A group of marauders, attracted by the scent of cooking food, descended upon the garden. The old survivalist, it seemed, had a few tricks up her sleeve. She dispatched the marauders with a combination of cunning and lethal force, but not before they set fire to the surrounding foliage. As the flames spread, Midas and Chewy made their escape, the old survivalist's parting gift – a small, precious bottle of antibiotics – clutched in Midas's hand. Chewy's eyes flashed a relieved, soft pink as they stumbled back toward their base, the inferno raging behind them. As they collapsed onto their makeshift bed, exhausted and battered, Midas turned to Chewy and grinned. "Well, that was a day." Chewy's eyes flickered a wry, orange-yellow, a silent acknowledgement that, indeed, it had been a very long, very eventful day.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This post-apocalyptic buddy story attempts to capture Terry Pratchett's distinctive voice but falls short in several key areas. The premise is charming - a hapless survivor paired with an animatronic koala whose color-changing eyes serve as emotional commentary - and shows creative potential. However, the execution reveals significant weaknesses. The Pratchett-style voice is inconsistent and often absent. While there are moments of dry observation ("a testament to the ingenuity of pre-Apocalypse construction"), the prose lacks Pratchett's characteristic wit, philosophical asides, and clever wordplay. The narrative voice feels more like generic post-apocalyptic fiction than the requested wry, dry style. The story structure follows the prompt adequately - deliberation, mission gone wrong, return home worse for wear - but the execution feels rushed and episodic. Events happen in rapid succession without proper development: rival scavenger, giant rat, garden owner, marauders, fire. Each encounter feels like a video game level rather than meaningful story beats. Character development is minimal. Midas remains a cipher throughout, defined only by his tendency toward trouble. Chewy's color-changing eyes are a clever device but become repetitive and mechanical rather than genuinely expressive. The supporting characters (rival scavenger, old survivalist) are stock types without depth. The dialogue is sparse and when present, lacks personality or wit. Conversations feel functional rather than character-revealing. The old survivalist's speech ("This ain't no charity") reads as generic tough-survivor dialogue. The prose suffers from tell-don't-show tendencies, particularly in describing emotions and reactions through Chewy's eye colors rather than showing tension through action and dialogue. Descriptions are workmanlike but lack vivid imagery or memorable details. The pacing feels rushed, cramming multiple encounters into limited space without allowing any to breathe or develop properly. The ending, while not inappropriately positive, feels abrupt and unearned - the characters haven't grown or changed meaningfully through their ordeal. The story shows competent basic writing skills but lacks the sophistication, humor, and distinctive voice that would make it memorable or truly engaging. + Romance: Love in the Limelight — Score: 39.8
Prompt:
Romance: Love in the Limelight. Write one scene within a larger story set in Wales. A famous (fictional) actor ducks into a small-town bookstore to escape paparazzi. The scene takes us through the characters meeting in this odd circumstance. Over the course of the scene, the actor and the bookstore owner have a conversation charged by an undercurrent of unspoken chemistry. Write the actor as somewhat of a rogue with a fragile ego, which needs to be fed by having everyone like him. He is thoroughly charming, but the bookstore owner seems (at least superficially) immune to this; which paradoxically provokes a genuine attraction and derails the charm offensive. The bookstore owner, despite the superficial rebuffs of the actor's charm, is inwardly more than a little charmed and flustered despite themselves. Write primarily in dialogue, in the distinct voices of each character. 1000 words.
Model Output:
**Scene: "A Haven from the Storm"** Rhys Williams, Hollywood's latest heartthrob, ducked into the cozy bookstore, dodging the paparazzi swarming outside. He had been in Cardiff for a film shoot and the local press had been relentless in their pursuit of a scoop. The sign above the door read "Cwtch Books" – a Welsh word for "hug" – and Rhys hoped it would provide the sanctuary he desperately needed. As he entered, a bell above the door jingled, and the owner, Emilia Jenkins, looked up from behind the counter, where she was surrounded by stacks of books and a steaming cup of tea. Her eyes narrowed slightly as she took in Rhys's disheveled appearance – his hair mussed, his eyes sunken from lack of sleep, and a hint of desperation etched on his face. "Can I help you?" Emilia asked, her tone neutral, but her eyes sparkling with curiosity. Rhys flashed his famous smile, the one that had won over millions of fans worldwide. "Just looking for a refuge from the storm outside. I'm a big fan of books, you know." Emilia raised an eyebrow. "Really? Which ones?" Rhys hesitated, realizing he hadn't actually read a book in years, aside from film scripts. "Uh, well, I'm more of a... a poetry man. Yeah, that's it. Poetry." Emilia's expression remained skeptical. "Poetry, huh? We have a great selection of Welsh poets. Would you like me to show you some?" Rhys's smile faltered for a moment, but he quickly recovered. "No, no, I think I'll just browse. You know, get a feel for the place." As Rhys wandered the aisles, running his fingers over the spines of the books, Emilia watched him with a mixture of amusement and suspicion. She had seen his type before – charming, self-absorbed, and used to getting his way. But there was something about Rhys that piqued her interest, maybe the vulnerability he tried to hide behind his cocky facade. After a few minutes of browsing, Rhys returned to the counter, holding a slim volume of Dylan Thomas's poetry. "You know, I think I'll take this one. I've always been a fan of his work." Emilia raised an eyebrow as she rang up the sale. "Really? Which poem is your favorite?" Rhys hesitated, unsure of how to respond. He had never actually read any of Thomas's work, but he had heard the name bandied about at parties. "Uh, well, I think it's... uh... 'Do Not Go Gentle into That Good Night'?" Emilia's eyes sparkled with amusement. "That's a popular choice. But I think my favorite is 'Fern Hill'. There's something about the way he captures the essence of Welsh childhood that resonates with me." Rhys felt a pang of embarrassment at being caught out, but he quickly recovered, launching into a charming anecdote about his own childhood. Emilia listened, her expression softening, but her eyes still sparkling with skepticism. As they chatted, the paparazzi outside began to disperse, and the stormy weather subsided, but Rhys lingered, reluctant to leave the warm, cozy atmosphere of the bookstore – and Emilia's presence. As he prepared to leave, Emilia handed him a small package. "I threw in a few extras – some Welsh cakes and a bookmark with a quote from 'Fern Hill'. I think you might appreciate it." Rhys's eyes met Emilia's, and for a moment, they just looked at each other, the air charged with unspoken chemistry. Rhys, usually confident in his ability to charm anyone, felt a flutter in his chest as Emilia's gaze seemed to see right through him. "Thanks," he said, his voice softer than he intended. "I appreciate it." Emilia smiled, a small, enigmatic smile. "Just be sure to read it, okay?" Rhys nodded, feeling a strange sense of connection to this small-town bookstore owner. As he left the shop, he glanced back over his shoulder, catching Emilia's eye. For a moment, they just looked at each other, the connection between them crackling like electricity. Rhys's charm offensive had been derailed, but he couldn't help feeling that he had stumbled into something much more interesting – a genuine connection with someone who saw past his facade to the vulnerable person beneath. And he couldn't wait to see Emilia again, to explore this unexpected attraction and discover what lay beneath her reserved exterior.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to fulfill the prompt's requirements but falls short in several key areas. The setup is competent - a famous actor seeking refuge from paparazzi in a Welsh bookstore - and the basic character dynamics are established. However, the execution reveals significant weaknesses. The dialogue, which was meant to be the primary vehicle for the story, feels stilted and unnatural. Conversations don't flow organically, and the characters' voices lack distinctiveness. Rhys's attempts at charm come across as generic rather than roguishly appealing, while Emilia's responses feel more like plot devices than authentic reactions from a real person. The piece suffers from excessive telling rather than showing. Instead of allowing readers to infer the chemistry and character traits through action and subtext, the narrative explicitly states emotions and motivations. Phrases like "the air charged with unspoken chemistry" and "his cocky facade" remove subtlety and reader engagement. Character development is superficial. Rhys's fragile ego is mentioned but not convincingly portrayed through his actions or dialogue. His embarrassment at being caught out about Dylan Thomas is handled clumsily, and his recovery feels too easy. Emilia's supposed immunity to his charm isn't well-demonstrated - she seems mildly skeptical rather than genuinely unimpressed. The Welsh setting feels tokenistic rather than integral. Beyond the bookstore name "Cwtch Books" and mentions of Welsh poets, there's little sense of place or cultural authenticity. The dialogue doesn't reflect distinct Welsh voices or speech patterns. The romantic tension lacks genuine spark. The "unspoken chemistry" is repeatedly stated but never convincingly established through meaningful interaction or subtext. The ending feels rushed and unearned, with both characters suddenly experiencing profound connection based on minimal interaction. Structurally, the piece meanders without building sufficient tension or momentum. The paparazzi threat disappears too easily, removing external pressure that could have heightened the scene's stakes.
