+ Fanfic-crossover: Prison Strings — Score: 52.2
Prompt:
Prison Strings Jolyne Cujoh & Makima Write a story where Jolyne Cujoh (JoJo's Bizarre Adventure) and Makima (Chainsaw Man) cross paths at a supernatural prison facility. Jolyne is immediately suspicious of Makima's falsely sweet demeanor, while Makima is intrigued by Jolyne's Stand ability. Their battle of wits escalates dangerously as Jolyne realizes how manipulative Makima truly is. **Jolyne Cujoh (JoJo's Bizarre Adventure)** Jolyne is the daughter of Jotaro Kujo and the first female JoJo protagonist. Her Stand, Stone Free, allows her to unravel her body into string that she can control. She's hot-headed, foul-mouthed, and doesn't take disrespect from anyone. She was framed for murder and sent to prison. She has a distinctive butterfly tattoo on her arm and wears her hair in two buns. Despite her tough exterior, she's deeply loyal to her friends and family. She can be impulsive but is highly adaptable in battle. She inherited her father's ability to stay cool under pressure but is more emotionally expressive. Famous quote: "If there's no Mickey, this shit ain't Disney!" **Makima (Chainsaw Man)** Makima appears as a young woman with auburn hair and ringed yellow eyes. She's the Control Devil who can dominate anyone she considers beneath her (nearly everyone). She maintains a pleasant, soft-spoken demeanor that masks her manipulative, cold nature. She can create contracts with humans and devils, often exploiting their desires. She's obsessed with Chainsaw Man and wants to control him. She keeps numerous people and devils as pets on leashes. She's practically immortal due to a contract with the Prime Minister. She views humans as lesser beings but mimics human emotions perfectly. Famous quote: "It's okay. Dogs are supposed to die for their owners." Third person, present tense. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
The sun beats down on the supernatural prison facility, casting a harsh glare over the chain-link fences and watchtowers. Jolyne Cujoh, her distinctive butterfly tattoo visible on her arm, walks down the yard with a confident stride, her two buns bobbing with each step. Her eyes scan the surroundings, ever vigilant for potential threats. She's been in this hellhole for months, framed for a murder she didn't commit, and she's not about to let her guard down. As she approaches the prison's central hub, she notices a commotion near the entrance. A group of inmates are staring at a newcomer, their faces a mix of awe and fear. Jolyne's curiosity gets the better of her, and she saunters over to see what the fuss is about. That's when she sees her: Makima, the Control Devil, with her auburn hair and ringed yellow eyes. Makima's smile is warm and inviting, but Jolyne's instincts scream warning. There's something off about this woman, something that doesn't add up. Makima's gaze locks onto Jolyne, and she glides towards her with an unnerving elegance. "Ah, you must be Jolyne Cujoh," Makima says, her voice dripping with honey. "I've heard so much about you. It's a pleasure to finally meet you." Jolyne's eyes narrow. She doesn't buy the act for a second. "What do you want, Makima?" she asks, her tone firm but wary. Makima's smile never wavers. "Oh, I just wanted to introduce myself. I'm a bit of a... collector, you might say. I'm always on the lookout for interesting individuals, and I must say, your... abilities are quite fascinating." Jolyne's grip on her Stone Free string tightens. She doesn't like where this is going. "What do you know about my abilities?" Makima's eyes sparkle with curiosity. "I know that your Stand, Stone Free, allows you to unravel your body into string. It's quite... unique. I'd love to learn more about it." Jolyne's instincts are screaming at her to be cautious. She doesn't trust Makima as far as she can throw her. "I don't think that's any of your business," she says, her tone cold. Makima's smile grows wider. "Oh, but it is. You see, I have a bit of a... proposition for you, Jolyne. I think we could help each other out. I could use someone with your... talents, and I'm willing to offer you a deal." Jolyne's eyes flash with anger. "What kind of deal?" Makima's gaze never leaves Jolyne's face. "I can offer you freedom, Jolyne. I can get you out of this prison and back into the world. All you have to do is agree to work with me." Jolyne's laughter is bitter. "You think I'm that easy to buy? I'm not some naive little girl who's going to fall for your tricks." Makima's expression never changes, but Jolyne senses a flicker of annoyance behind her eyes. "Oh, I think you'll find that my offers are quite... generous, Jolyne. And I always get what I want." The air between them grows thick with tension as the two women engage in a silent battle of wills. Jolyne knows that Makima is hiding something, that there's more to her proposal than meets the eye. She's determined to uncover the truth, no matter what it takes. As the standoff continues, the inmates around them begin to disperse, sensing the danger emanating from the two women. The chain-link fences seem to rattle in anticipation, as if they know that a storm is brewing. Jolyne's eyes never leave Makima's face. "I'm not interested in your deal," she says, her voice firm. "And I'm not afraid of you." Makima's smile grows wider, her eyes glinting with amusement. "Oh, but you should be, Jolyne. You should be very afraid." The tension between them is palpable, a living, breathing thing that threatens to consume them both. Jolyne knows that she's in for the fight of her life, and she's ready to take on Makima and her manipulative games. The question is, will she emerge victorious, or will she become Makima's latest pawn?

+ Scp: Notes from the Future — Score: 45.7
Prompt:
Write an SCP report about a researcher who begins finding handwritten notes from their future self, warning about a containment breach that hasn't happened yet. The notes become increasingly desperate and incoherent, sometimes containing information that contradicts known reality. Include the Foundation's attempts to determine if this is an actual temporal anomaly or psychological manipulation by a contained entity, and the researcher's struggle to trust their own perception. First person (researcher's perspective with interspersed notes), past tense. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**SCP-XXXX: "The Notes of Tomorrow"** **Incident Report** I still remember the day I found the first note. It was a typical Tuesday morning at Site-17, and I was sipping my coffee while reviewing the day's schedule. That's when I saw it - a small piece of paper on my desk with a handwritten message: "Containment breach imminent. Do not trust Dr. Kim." I was taken aback. Who could have written this, and how did they get into my office? I showed it to my colleagues, but no one recognized the handwriting. We brushed it off as a prank, but the message stuck with me. Over the next few days, I found more notes. They were always in the same handwriting, and always seemed to appear out of nowhere. " SCP-173 is not what you think it is. Do not approach." "Trust no one. The breach is coming." At first, I thought it was just a clever prank or a psychological experiment gone wrong. But as the notes continued to appear, I started to feel a sense of unease. Who was writing these, and how did they know about our research? As a researcher, I've worked with my fair share of anomalous objects and entities. But this was different. These notes seemed to be coming from...myself. Or at least, a version of myself from the future. I began to analyze the notes, looking for any clues that might explain what was happening. The ink used was a custom blend, not matching any office pen. The paper was a standard issue, but the way it was folded and creased suggested that it had been handled by someone who was in a hurry. As the notes continued to appear, they became increasingly desperate and incoherent. "THEY'RE COMING FOR YOU. HIDE THE KETTLE." "SCP-682 IS NOT THE WORST. WAIT FOR THE OTHER." I started to feel like I was losing my grip on reality. Were these notes really from my future self, or was I just experiencing some kind of psychological breakdown? I brought the notes to the attention of my superiors, and they launched an investigation. We ran psychological evaluations, checked for any signs of manipulation by a contained entity, and even conducted a sweep of the site for any signs of anomalous activity. But nothing turned up. It was as if I was the only one who saw these notes. As the days went by, the notes became more frequent and more urgent. "IT'S TOO LATE. THE BREACH IS HAPPENING. ABDUCT SCP-087." "YOU'LL NEVER MAKE IT. THE CLOCK IS TICKING." I started to feel like I was trapped in some kind of temporal loop, reliving the same moments over and over. I couldn't shake the feeling that I was running out of time. One of the notes mentioned a specific date and time - 3:47 AM on March 15th. I circled it on my calendar, wondering what would happen on that day. As the day approached, I became increasingly anxious. Would the breach really happen? And if so, what could I do to stop it? On the night of March 14th, I couldn't sleep. I kept checking my clock, waiting for the moment when...whatever was supposed to happen, would happen. At 3:47 AM, I received a call from the site's emergency response team. There had been a containment breach. SCP-087 had escaped, and several researchers were injured. I felt a chill run down my spine. The note had been right. But as I rushed to the scene, I realized that something was off. The breach had been caused by a faulty door seal, not by any anomalous activity. And the researchers who were injured were not the ones I had expected. It was as if the notes had been trying to tell me something, but not what I thought. Or maybe, just maybe, I had been manipulated all along. I'm still trying to make sense of it all. Were the notes really from my future self, or was it just a clever ploy by a contained entity? I may never know for sure. But one thing is certain - I'll never look at a piece of paper the same way again. **Addendum:** Following the incident, the researcher was placed on administrative leave and underwent a thorough psychological evaluation. The results were inconclusive, but the researcher's access to sensitive information was restricted. The anomalous nature of the notes remains unclear, and the Foundation continues to monitor the situation. **Note:** The researcher's calendar was found with the date and time of the breach circled, along with several other dates and times that correspond to unexplained events at the site. The significance of these markings is still being investigated.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to fulfill the SCP format requirements but falls short in several key areas. The writing follows a basic first-person narrative structure as requested, but lacks the clinical precision and documentation style that makes SCP reports compelling. The format is inconsistent - it begins as an "Incident Report" but reads more like a personal journal entry. The temporal anomaly concept is present but underdeveloped. The notes from the future self are too generic and lack the specific, unsettling details that would make them feel authentically anomalous. Examples like "HIDE THE KETTLE" feel random rather than mysteriously significant. The progression from coherent to incoherent notes is attempted but not executed convincingly. The researcher's psychological journey is superficial. While the prompt calls for a struggle with perception and trust, the protagonist's internal conflict feels perfunctory rather than genuinely distressing. The writing tells us the character feels anxious and confused but doesn't effectively show this deterioration through voice, behavior, or increasingly unreliable narration. The Foundation's investigation is mentioned but barely explored. There's no sense of the institutional response, scientific methodology, or the bureaucratic machinery that defines SCP fiction. The resolution is weak - the containment breach occurs but feels coincidental rather than meaningfully connected to the temporal anomaly. The prose is workmanlike but lacks atmosphere. SCP fiction thrives on clinical detachment punctuated by moments of cosmic horror, but this piece maintains a mundane tone throughout. The dialogue is minimal and unremarkable. The pacing meanders without building tension effectively. The ending attempts ambiguity about whether the phenomenon is real or psychological manipulation, but this uncertainty feels unearned because neither possibility was developed with sufficient depth or evidence. + Scp: Unmarked Doors Archive — Score: 57.5
Prompt:
Write an SCP entry about a series of identical unmarked doors appearing in abandoned buildings worldwide that lead to a massive, architecturally impossible archive. Documents within reference a previous global civilization destroyed by an unspecified containment failure. Foundation researchers discover references to their own organization under a different name, including personnel files for current staff dated centuries ago. Include exploration logs revealing sections of the archive actively being removed by entities resembling hazmat teams who flee when approached, and evidence that O5 Council members have visited the archive without authorization. Third person (exploration team perspective) with recovered document excerpts. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**SCP-XXXX: "The Archive of Echoes"** Object Class: Euclid Special Containment Procedures: Mobile Task Forces are to be dispatched to investigate and secure any newly discovered instances of SCP-XXXX. All entrances to SCP-XXXX are to be sealed and monitored for unauthorized access. Foundation personnel are prohibited from accessing SCP-XXXX without Level 3 clearance and approval from at least two Level 4 personnel. O5 Council members are specifically barred from accessing SCP-XXXX without explicit permission from the entire Council. Description: SCP-XXXX refers to a series of identical, unmarked doors that have appeared in abandoned buildings worldwide. These doors are always located in areas inaccessible to the general public, such as abandoned attics, basements, or disused stairwells. The doors themselves are plain, metallic, and lack any visible locking mechanism. Upon opening an SCP-XXXX door, individuals will find themselves in a massive, labyrinthine archive. The architecture of the archive is impossible according to current understanding, with rooms and corridors shifting and folding in ways that defy spatial logic. The archive contains millions of documents, files, and records, all detailing the history and workings of a previously unknown global civilization. Document excerpts recovered from SCP-XXXX: * "…The Great Error of 1873, in which a containment breach at the Parisian Hub led to the downfall of our civilization. The subsequent [REDACTED] protocols were unable to mitigate the damage, and our world was lost to the void." * "…The Order of the New Dawn, a coalition of nations dedicated to containing and researching anomalous phenomena. Their legacy lives on in the modern [REDACTED] Foundation, but their methods are far more… draconian." * "…Personnel File: Dr. Elara Vex, Chief Researcher, Department of Anomalous Physics. Date of Birth: 1856. Date of Death: 1923. Current Assignment: Lead Researcher, SCP-XXXX." Exploration Log XXXX-1: **Date:**//20 **Team:** MTF-XXXX-1 ("The Archivists") **Objective:** Explore the SCP-XXXX archive, gather information on the previous civilization, and assess potential risks. Upon entering the archive, we immediately noticed the sheer scale of the repository. Rows upon rows of shelves stretched out before us, laden with documents, files, and artifacts. We began to search for any mention of the current Foundation, and were shocked to discover references to our organization under the name "The Order of the New Dawn." Further research revealed that many current Foundation personnel have "personnel files" within the archive, despite being born centuries after the supposed downfall of the previous civilization. As we delved deeper into the archive, we encountered entities resembling hazmat teams, clad in black and orange suits, actively removing sections of the archive. When approached, these entities fled, leaving behind scattered documents and cryptic notes. Exploration Log XXXX-2: **Date:**//20 **Team:** MTF-XXXX-1 ("The Archivists") **Objective:** Investigate the entities removing archive sections, and gather more information on the previous civilization. We tracked the entities to a section of the archive dedicated to the "Great Error of 1873." The documents within detailed a catastrophic containment breach that led to the downfall of the previous civilization. As we read through the records, we noticed that several key pages were missing, and the remaining text seemed to be redacted. Suddenly, the entities reappeared, this time accompanied by a figure in a black suit and tie. They approached us, and the figure revealed himself to be O5-█, a high-ranking member of the Foundation's governing Council. O5-█: "I'm afraid you're not cleared for this level of access. You will leave now, and forget what you've seen." We were escorted out of the archive, and our memories of the encounter were subsequently altered. Further investigation revealed that multiple O5 Council members have visited SCP-XXXX without authorization, sparking concerns about potential breaches of protocol and the true nature of the Foundation's involvement with the archive. Addendum: Following Incident XXXX-1, all O5 Council members have been barred from accessing SCP-XXXX. Mobile Task Forces have been instructed to monitor the archive for any further unauthorized access, and to report any changes in the entities' behavior or the archive's contents.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This SCP entry demonstrates a solid understanding of the Foundation universe's format and tone, successfully incorporating the clinical, bureaucratic style characteristic of SCP documentation. The piece adheres well to the prompt's requirements, including the mysterious doors, impossible archive, references to a previous civilization, personnel files for current staff, hazmat-suited entities, and unauthorized O5 visits. The writing maintains consistency in voice throughout, employing the expected third-person clinical perspective with appropriate redactions and formal language. The structure follows SCP conventions effectively, moving from containment procedures through description to exploration logs and addenda. However, the piece suffers from several notable weaknesses. The exploration logs feel rushed and lack the detailed, methodical approach typical of high-quality SCP entries. The encounter with O5-█ is particularly abrupt and unconvincing - the dialogue feels stilted and the resolution too convenient. The memory alteration explanation serves as a weak narrative device that undermines the tension built up in the discovery. The descriptive quality is adequate but not exceptional. While the archive's impossible architecture is mentioned, it lacks vivid detail that would make the space feel genuinely otherworldly or threatening. The entities are described generically as "hazmat teams" without distinctive characteristics that would make them memorable or unsettling. The piece shows creativity in connecting the current Foundation to a previous civilization through the "Order of the New Dawn," but this concept isn't fully developed. The "Great Error of 1873" is intriguing but remains frustratingly vague, even by SCP standards. The implications of current staff having centuries-old personnel files could have been explored more deeply. The writing tends toward tell-don't-show, particularly in the exploration logs where events are summarized rather than experienced. The emotional impact is limited, lacking the existential dread or cosmic horror that characterizes the best SCP entries. The ending feels somewhat anticlimactic, with the containment procedures updated but no real resolution to the deeper mysteries presented. + Classic sci-fi: Offworlder (Le Guin) — Score: 48.7
Prompt:
Classic sci-fi: Offworlder (Author style: Le Guin) Write a chapter following a young diplomatic envoy sent to address tensions on a distant human colony where humanity has diverged into distinct subspecies through both natural adaptation and separation of lineages. Against protocol, the envoy slips away from official functions to walk the streets alone, encountering markets, ordinary citizens, and social structures that contradict the official briefings. Upon returning to their quarters, the envoy is reprimanded by Command, and is tasked with approaching the stationed Minister of Science (a political posting rather than scientific). A challenging conversation ensues, in which the envoy's wits and will are tested, by a seasoned political operator looking to test the mettle of the offworlder. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
Chapter 5: The Unseen Streets Envoy Kaelin Vex slipped away from the ceremonial procession, shedding the suffocating protocol like a worn cloak. The humid air enveloped her as she stepped into the narrow alleys of New Elysium's lower districts. The scent of exotic spices and fresh bread wafted through the crowded market, enticing her senses. For the first time since arrival, Kaelin felt alive. Her official attire, a flowing black cloak with intricate silver embroidery, drew curious stares from locals who dressed more minimally in lightweight tunics and leggings. The colonists' adaptations to the planet's harsh environment had led to distinct physical characteristics, such as the striking iridescent skin of the native-born Elysians. Kaelin's own features, honed from generations of offworlders, seemed almost bland in comparison. As she navigated the winding alleys, Kaelin discovered a world that contradicted the polished briefings and sterile diplomatic functions. She saw families huddled around cooking fires, sharing meals and laughter. Street performers juggled glowing orbs, their faces painted with vibrant patterns that shimmered in the fading light. Everywhere, the sounds of haggling merchants and the hum of hover-drones filled the air. Kaelin's trained eyes absorbed the details, her mind racing with the implications. The official narrative spoke of a unified colony, but the streets told a different story. She saw signs of tension, of subtle divisions between the native-born and the offworlder settlers. The intricate social structures, the unspoken hierarchies, and the hidden power dynamics all whispered secrets in her ear. As night began to fall, Kaelin reluctantly returned to her quarters, a modest suite within the diplomatic compound. She was greeted by a stern-faced aide, who handed her a comms device with a flicker of annoyance. "Commander Ortega requests your presence, Envoy," the aide said, her voice laced with a hint of warning. Kaelin's heart sank as she accepted the device. She knew she had overstepped protocol by venturing into the city unescorted. "Envoy Vex, this is Commander Ortega. Your... excursion into the city has raised concerns. You are to report to Minister Arin Vashin immediately. He wishes to discuss your... observations." Kaelin's eyes narrowed. Minister Vashin was a political posting, not a scientist. This was not a meeting she was looking forward to. The Minister's office was a labyrinth of gleaming white corridors and polished obsidian panels. Kaelin was ushered into a spacious chamber with a breathtaking view of the city's sprawling metropolis. Minister Vashin, a tall, imposing figure with piercing blue eyes, rose from behind his desk to greet her. "Envoy Vex, welcome. I trust your... excursion into our fair city was enlightening?" His tone was laced with a subtle challenge. Kaelin met his gaze, her expression neutral. "I gained valuable insights, Minister. The city is... vibrant. However, I did notice certain... discrepancies between the official briefings and the reality on the ground." Vashin's smile was a thin-lipped thing. "Ah, yes. The 'reality on the ground.' A diplomat's euphemism for 'things we'd rather not discuss.' Tell me, Envoy, what exactly did you see that so... intrigued you?" Kaelin chose her words carefully, aware that the Minister was probing for weaknesses. "I observed signs of social tension, Minister. The native-born Elysians seem to be... segregated from the offworlder settlers. I saw evidence of economic disparities, and a sense of disconnection between the various districts." Vashin leaned back in his chair, steepling his fingers. "And what, pray tell, do you propose we do about these... 'discrepancies'?" Kaelin's instincts warned her that the Minister was testing her, pushing her to reveal her true intentions. She took a deep breath and plunged forward. "I propose, Minister, that we engage in open and honest dialogue with the Elysian people. We must acknowledge the historical grievances and work towards reconciliation. The offworlder settlers and the native-born must be brought together, their voices heard and their concerns addressed." Vashin's expression turned glacial. "You are a diplomat, Envoy, not a social engineer. Your role is to facilitate cooperation, not to impose your own brand of... 'justice.' We have a delicate balance to maintain here. I suggest you focus on the task at hand, rather than trying to reshape our society to fit your... ideals." Kaelin's will was tested, but she refused to back down. "With respect, Minister, I am not here to impose my own ideals. I am here to facilitate understanding and cooperation. The people of New Elysium deserve a voice, and it is our duty as diplomats to listen." The Minister's eyes seemed to bore into her very soul, searching for any sign of weakness. Kaelin stood firm, her gaze locked on his, as the silence between them stretched like a challenge. Finally, Vashin spoke, his voice dripping with condescension. "I see. Well, Envoy, it seems we have a long way to go in... educating you about the realities of our world. I suggest you focus on the diplomatic functions, and leave the... 'social engineering' to those of us who truly understand this planet." Kaelin's face remained impassive, but her mind seethed with determination. She would not be swayed, nor would she back down. The people of New Elysium deserved better, and she was determined to be their voice.
Judge Evaluation:

+ Biopunk: Polymerase Chain Reaction — Score: 68.8
Prompt:
Biopunk -- Polymerase Chain Reaction Write a chapter set in a near-future post-apocalyptic world where corporate genetic engineering was designed with built-in obsolescence—engineered DNA lasting only one generation to maximize profits before societal collapse. Follow a biohacker working with salvaged equipment to splice viable food crops for their settlement using rapidly degrading genetic material. As world building / window dressing, include details about jury-rigged lab equipment, and the physical toll (and unexpected upsides) of using untested genetic modifications as medicine. The plot of this chapter is centred around a black market contract. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
Chapter 7: Splicing Hope The dim glow of the salvaged LED strips illuminated the cramped, makeshift lab. Dr. Samantha "Sam" Taylor hunched over the rickety workbench, her eyes fixed on the microscope's eyepiece. The air was thick with the smell of burnt plastic and ozone, a constant reminder of the jury-rigged equipment that kept her research alive. A faint hum emanated from the repurposed 3D printer, now serving as a makeshift thermocycler for her Polymerase Chain Reaction (PCR) experiments. Sam's current project was a high-stakes game: splicing viable food crops from the rapidly degrading genetic material of the pre-Collapse era. The once-mighty biotech corporations had designed their products with built-in obsolescence, ensuring that the engineered DNA would last only one generation. The strategy had maximized profits, but at the cost of a sustainable future. Now, in the ravaged world, Sam's biohacking skills were the only hope for her settlement's survival. A knock on the lab's makeshift door interrupted her focus. Sam's assistant, Jax, poked his head in, his eyes scanning the cluttered space. "Sam, we've got a visitor. Says he's from the...other side." Sam's grip on the pipette tightened. "What does he want?" Jax hesitated before answering, "He's looking for a custom splice. High-paying job, but...there's a catch." Sam raised an eyebrow. "What kind of catch?" Jax leaned in, his voice barely above a whisper. "He wants us to use the 'Eclipse' strain. You know, the one from the black market?" Sam's eyes widened. The Eclipse strain was infamous for its unpredictable effects on the human body. Some said it granted temporary boosts in strength and agility, while others whispered about its link to the mysterious "Ghost Sickness" that had been plaguing the settlements. "What's the job?" Sam asked, her curiosity piqued. "He wants us to create a crop that's resistant to the 'Devouring Fungus'," Jax replied, referring to the deadly pathogen that had been decimating the remaining food sources. "But here's the thing: he needs it to be compatible with the Eclipse strain. Whatever that means." Sam's mind racing, she weighed the risks and benefits. The payoff could be substantial, potentially securing her settlement's future for years to come. But at what cost? The Eclipse strain was a genetic wild card, and tampering with it could have disastrous consequences. "I'll take the job," Sam said finally, a sense of determination washing over her. "But I need to know more about the client and what he's planning. Get him to agree to a meeting, and make sure he understands the risks involved." Jax nodded and disappeared into the dimly lit corridor, leaving Sam to ponder the implications of her decision. She glanced around the lab, her gaze settling on the empty canisters from the defunct biotech giant, now serving as makeshift reagent containers. The irony wasn't lost on her – using the remnants of a system designed to control and exploit to create something that could potentially bring about positive change. As she waited for the mysterious client to arrive, Sam couldn't shake off the feeling that she was playing with fire. The Eclipse strain was a ticking time bomb, and she was about to add fuel to the flames. The door creaked open, and a hooded figure stepped into the lab. Sam's eyes locked onto the stranger, her mind racing with questions. Who was this person, and what did they plan to do with the custom splice? "Let's get down to business," the figure said, its voice distorted by a vocal modulator. "I have a proposition for you, Dr. Taylor. One that could change the course of our little settlement's history." Sam steeled herself, ready to face whatever lay ahead. The fate of her people hung in the balance, and she was willing to take the risk. But as she looked into the stranger's obscured face, she couldn't help but wonder: was she about to make a deal with a benefactor, or a devil?
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This biopunk chapter demonstrates solid adherence to the prompt's requirements, establishing a post-apocalyptic world where corporate genetic engineering with built-in obsolescence has led to societal collapse. The author successfully incorporates the requested elements: a biohacker protagonist working with salvaged equipment, degrading genetic material, and a black market contract as the central plot driver. The worldbuilding shows competent execution with details like repurposed 3D printers serving as thermocyclers, salvaged LED strips for lighting, and defunct biotech containers repurposed as reagent holders. These details effectively convey the jury-rigged nature of the laboratory without becoming overly technical or losing narrative momentum. Character-wise, Sam Taylor emerges as a believable protagonist whose actions align with her expertise and circumstances. Her decision-making process regarding the dangerous Eclipse strain contract feels authentic to someone balancing survival needs against scientific ethics. However, the characterization remains somewhat surface-level, with limited psychological depth or distinctive voice. The prose maintains a consistent tone throughout, balancing technical terminology with accessible narrative. The writing flows naturally and avoids major stylistic pitfalls, though it occasionally relies on familiar genre tropes (mysterious hooded figures, ominous strain names like "Eclipse" and "Ghost Sickness"). The dialogue, while functional, lacks distinctiveness. Characters speak in fairly generic ways that don't reveal much personality or background. The mysterious client's final lines feel particularly conventional for the cyberpunk/biopunk genre. The chapter effectively builds tension around the moral dilemma of accepting dangerous work for survival, though the stakes and consequences could be more vividly rendered. The ending appropriately sets up future conflict without resolving prematurely, though the "deal with the devil" framing is somewhat predictable. Notable weaknesses include limited exploration of the "physical toll and unexpected upsides" of genetic modifications as medicine (mentioned in the prompt but barely addressed), and some reliance on telling rather than showing, particularly regarding the Eclipse strain's effects and the settlement's dire circumstances. + Classic sci-fi: The Azra Gambit — Score: 68.0
Prompt:
Classic sci-fi (Author style: Asimov) The Azra Gambit Colonial mars is being mined by corporations who take leases on indentured labourers. The thing they are mining is Azra, a recently discovered exotic metal which accelerates radioactive decay to such a rate that it is greatly sought after for interstellar drives and weapons alike. This has created both a gold rush and an arms race as various interests vie for control and endeavour to unlock Azra's secrets. The story follows Arthur Neegan, a first generation settler and mining engineer. Upon discovering that his unassuming plot sits atop an immense Azra vein, he is subjected to a flurry of interest and scrutiny. Write the next chapter in this story, in which an armed retinue descends on Arthur's home and politely but forcefully invites him to a meeting with some unknown party off-world. The insignia look like that of the Antares diplomatic corp -- diplomatic in name only. Arthur finds himself in the centre of a political tug of war. The chapter involves a meeting with this unknown party, who makes Arthur an offer. The scene should be primarily dialogue, interspersed with vivid description & scene setting. It should sow hints of the larger intrigue, stakes & dangers. Include Asimov's trademark big-and-small-picture world building and retrofuturistic classic scifi vibe. The chapter begins with Arthur aboard the transfer vessel, wondering just what he's gotten involved in. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
Chapter 2: The Antares Envoy Arthur Neegan's stomach churned as the transfer vessel, a utilitarian cylinder with a worn, metallic sheen, accelerated towards its unknown destination. The armed retinue that had arrived at his doorstep, their Antares diplomatic corp insignia gleaming on their chest plates, had been polite but firm in their insistence that he accompany them. The words "diplomatic" and "envoy" had been used, but Arthur's instincts screamed that this was anything but a cordial meeting. The vessel's minimalist interior, a mesh of steel grating and cold, grey panels, seemed designed to discourage frivolous conversation. A holographic display above the pilot's station flickered with cryptic navigation data, casting an eerie glow over the cabin. Arthur's thoughts swirled with questions: What did they want from him? Why had they chosen him, a relatively unknown mining engineer, for this mysterious meeting? The vessel shuddered, and Arthur's gaze drifted to the small display screen on the wall. System diagnostics cycled through in a steady stream of green text: LIFE SUPPORT NOMINAL, GRAVITY COMPENSATION ONLINE, RADIATION SHIELDING WITHIN SAFE PARAMETERS... The hatch slid open, and a suited figure, their face obscured by a reflective visor, gestured for Arthur to follow. "We're arriving, Mr. Neegan. Please, come with me." Arthur rose, smoothing his worn coveralls, and trailed the figure through the vessel's cramped corridors. They emerged into a spacious, dimly lit chamber filled with the soft hum of machinery and the faint scent of ozone. A curved, transparent wall offered a breathtaking view of the stars, with the crimson globe of Mars hanging like a lantern in the distance. A figure, dressed in a tailored, black uniform adorned with the Antares insignia, stood at the far end of the room. Their features, chiseled and angular, seemed carved from the same stone as the Martian landscape. As Arthur approached, the figure turned, their eyes locking onto his with an unnerving intensity. "Arthur Neegan, welcome. I am Envoy Elara Vex, representing the interests of the Antares Combine." Her voice was low, smooth, and devoid of warmth. "Please, take a seat." Arthur sank into the offered chair, his mind racing with the implications of being summoned by a representative of the Antares Combine, a vast, interplanetary conglomerate rumored to wield significant influence in the highest echelons of the solar system's governments. "What can I do for you, Envoy Vex?" Arthur asked, trying to keep his tone neutral. Elara Vex smiled, the expression a thin, calculated line. "We're interested in your... situation, Mr. Neegan. Your discovery of the Azra vein on your property has created a certain... flux in the market. The Antares Combine is willing to make you a generous offer for the rights to that vein." Arthur's instincts screamed warning, but he played along, curious about the stakes. "What kind of offer?" "A substantial one, Mr. Neegan. We're willing to pay a premium for the rights to extract and process the Azra. Enough to set you up for life, comfortably." The figure's words were laced with an undercurrent of menace, a subtle implication that refusal would not be... advisable. Arthur's thoughts turned to the gold rush on Mars, the desperate scramble for control of the Azra deposits, and the whispers of an arms race brewing in the shadows. "I'm not sure I'm interested in selling," Arthur said, stalling for time. Elara Vex's smile never wavered. "I think you'll find our offer... persuasive, Mr. Neegan. The Antares Combine is not an organization to be trifled with. We have... extensive resources at our disposal. Resources that could make your life very... complicated, should you choose to decline our offer." The air seemed to thicken, heavy with unspoken threats. Arthur's mind reeled as he struggled to grasp the scope of the game being played out around him. He was a small-time mining engineer, caught in the crosshairs of forces that spanned the solar system. "I'll need time to consider," Arthur said, stalling, his thoughts racing with the implications of Elara Vex's words. The envoy's smile grew, a fraction wider. "I'm afraid time is a luxury you no longer have, Mr. Neegan. The Azra market is... volatile. Other interests are already circling, eager to claim the vein for themselves. I suggest you make your decision soon. Very soon." As Arthur hesitated, the stars outside seemed to twinkle with a sinister light, as if the very fabric of the universe was being reshaped by the forces of human ambition. He knew, in that moment, that he stood at the edge of a precipice, staring into an abyss of intrigue and deception, with the fate of Colonial Mars hanging precariously in the balance.
Judge Evaluation:

The pacing works well, building tension through the journey and meeting structure. The ending appropriately raises stakes without false positivity. The writing shows technical competence but lacks the intellectual depth, character complexity, and elegant simplicity that define Asimov's best work. It reads more like competent genre fiction than a true homage to the master's style. The piece succeeds as functional sci-fi storytelling but falls short of capturing Asimov's distinctive voice and philosophical depth. + Contemporary romance: Darkroom Revelations — Score: 50.2
Prompt:
Darkroom Revelations Write a first-person narrative from the perspective of Dani, a 25-year-old assertive art student known for her bold style and take-charge attitude in relationships. For the past semester, she's been quietly fascinated by Elliot (he/him), a 19-year-old boy in her experimental photography class. Dani has been intrigued by his unconventional masculinity: killer thrift-shop-nu-goth style, soft demeanour and quiet intellect. When they're paired for a final project requiring late nights in the darkroom, Elliot tentatively shares that he's been questioning his gender identity and expression. Set during one of these intimate darkroom sessions where the red light creates a confessional atmosphere. Explore Dani's complex attraction—her usual assertiveness complicated by her desire to protect Elliot's vulnerability, her excitement at witnessing his self-discovery, and her confusion about what this means for her own identity as someone typically attracted to more defined gender presentations. The narrative should capture the tender awkwardness of their conversations, Dani's internal struggle between taking charge and wanting to give Elliot agency, and the unexpected chemistry that develops as both find themselves in uncharted territory. 1000 words.
Model Output:
I stepped into the darkroom, the familiar scent of developer and fixer enveloping me like a warm hug. The red light cast an eerie glow, making the space feel like a confessional. Elliot was already there, his slender fingers drumming a rhythm on the counter as he hummed a soft tune. I smiled, recognizing the nervous habit. We'd been paired for this final project, and I had to admit, I was excited to spend more time with him. As I set up our equipment, Elliot caught my eye, his gaze darting away quickly. I felt a flutter in my chest, a mix of attraction and curiosity. His style was like nothing I'd ever seen – a mashup of goth and nu-goth, with a dash of androgyny that made my heart skip a beat. But it was more than just his aesthetic that drew me in; it was the quiet confidence he exuded, the sense that he was still figuring himself out, and I was eager to witness that journey. "Hey, Dani," he said, his voice low and smooth, "I was thinking we could try something new with this project. Experiment with some unconventional techniques." I raised an eyebrow, intrigued. "Like what?" Elliot hesitated, his eyes locking onto mine before darting away. "I don't know, just... something that pushes the boundaries, you know?" I nodded, sensing there was more to his suggestion than met the eye. "I love it. Let's do it." As we worked, the darkness and the chemical fumes created an intimate atmosphere, like we were sharing a secret. Elliot's humming grew softer, and I found myself swaying to the tune. Our conversation flowed easily, discussing art, music, and life. But beneath the surface, I sensed a tension, a hesitancy that made me wonder what he was holding back. It wasn't until we were waiting for our images to reveal in the chemical bath that Elliot spoke up, his voice barely above a whisper. "Dani, can I tell you something?" My instincts told me to take charge, to reassure him that everything would be okay. But something about his vulnerability made me pause, and I nodded instead. "Of course, Elliot. What is it?" He took a deep breath, his eyes fixed on the swirling chemicals. "I've been... questioning things. About myself, I mean." My heart skipped a beat as I realized what he was getting at. "What kind of things?" I asked, trying to sound nonchalant despite the excitement building inside me. Elliot's gaze drifted back to mine, and I saw a flicker of fear, of uncertainty. "My gender, I guess. I don't know if I'm... if I'm really a guy, or if that's just what I've been told I am." I felt a rush of emotions: excitement, curiosity, and a dash of confusion. I'd always been drawn to people with defined gender presentations, and Elliot's uncertainty threw me off balance. But as I looked into his eyes, I saw something there that I couldn't ignore – a deep-seated desire to be seen, to be understood. My assertiveness, my usual take-charge attitude, warred with a desire to protect his vulnerability. I didn't want to push him, to make him feel like he was on display. But at the same time, I was eager to explore this new territory with him, to see where it would take us. "Elliot, that takes a lot of courage to admit," I said, trying to sound calm. "I'm here for you, no matter what." He smiled, a small, tentative smile. "Thanks, Dani. Just talking about it makes me feel... lighter, I guess." As we waited for the images to develop, the silence between us grew comfortable, like a warm blanket. I found myself stealing glances at Elliot, his profile illuminated by the red light. His features were delicate, yet strong, and I felt a pang of attraction that I couldn't ignore. The chemicals began to work their magic, and our images started to reveal themselves. Elliot gasped as a particularly striking print emerged, and I felt a surge of pride. We worked in tandem, our movements fluid, like we'd been doing this for years. As we rinsed the prints and hung them to dry, Elliot turned to me, his eyes sparkling. "Thanks for listening, Dani. It means a lot to me." I smiled, feeling a sense of wonder. "Anytime, Elliot. We're in this together, okay?" The words felt like a promise, a commitment to this uncharted territory we were exploring. As we left the darkroom, the bright lights of the outside world felt jarring, but I knew that I was ready to face whatever came next, as long as Elliot was by my side. In that moment, I realized that my attraction to him wasn't just about his style or his intellect – it was about the sense of possibility that he embodied. Elliot was a question mark, a mystery waiting to be unraveled, and I was eager to be a part of his journey, to see where it would take us both. As we walked out of the darkroom, Elliot began to hum that soft tune again, and I found myself swaying to the beat, my heart pounding in time with his. I knew that I was in for a wild ride, one that would challenge everything I thought I knew about myself and my desires. But with Elliot by my side, I was ready to face whatever came next, one frame at a time.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to tackle a sensitive and complex scenario involving gender identity exploration within a romantic context. The narrative successfully establishes the darkroom setting and maintains the first-person perspective of Dani throughout. However, several significant weaknesses undermine its effectiveness. The characterization feels superficial and relies heavily on telling rather than showing. Dani's "assertive art student" personality is mentioned but rarely demonstrated through her actions or dialogue. Her internal conflict between taking charge and respecting Elliot's agency is stated explicitly but not convincingly portrayed through her behavior. The description of Elliot as having "killer thrift-shop-nu-goth style" and "unconventional masculinity" reads more like a character sheet than organic narrative detail. The dialogue lacks authenticity and depth. Conversations feel stilted and overly careful, particularly during the crucial gender identity revelation scene. Elliot's confession comes across as somewhat mechanical: "My gender, I guess. I don't know if I'm... if I'm really a guy, or if that's just what I've been told I am." This moment should be the emotional centerpiece but lacks the vulnerability and complexity the prompt demands. The prose contains numerous clichéd phrases ("warm hug," "heart skip a beat," "wild ride") and relies on generic romantic fiction tropes. The writing frequently tells us what characters are feeling rather than allowing us to experience it through their actions and reactions. Phrases like "I felt a rush of emotions: excitement, curiosity, and a dash of confusion" exemplify this tell-don't-show approach. The pacing feels rushed, particularly in how quickly Dani processes and accepts Elliot's revelation. Her internal struggle about her own identity and attraction patterns is mentioned but not deeply explored. The ending's optimistic tone feels somewhat unearned given the complexity of the situation and the brief timeframe of the narrative. The darkroom setting is adequately established but not fully utilized for its metaphorical potential. While the red light and chemical atmosphere are mentioned, they don't contribute meaningfully to the emotional landscape of the story. The piece does succeed in maintaining narrative coherence and avoiding offensive treatment of gender identity issues. However, it lacks the emotional depth, authentic dialogue, and nuanced character development that would make it truly compelling. + Contemporary romance / drama: Stolen Moments in Roma — Score: 43.7
Prompt:
Contemporary Romance / Drama: Stolen Moments in Roma. Write a series of interconnected short scenes and dialogues that span a single day in modern-day Rome, in narrative form. This will form the beginning of a larger story. Alessandra, a fiery, independent Roman woman who works as a motorcycle courier, nearly collides with Ben, a somewhat clumsy, overly polite British academic on sabbatical, who is engrossed in a guidebook near the Trevi Fountain. The initial encounter is a clash of cultures and personalities – Alessandra is all sharp wit and rapid-fire Italian, while Ben is flustered apologies and awkward attempts at speaking the language. However, as they sort out the near-miss, a spark of unexpected humor and connection emerges. Alessandra, it quickly becomes clear, is a whirlwind of energy and mischief. She's a self-admitted troublemaker with a secret penchant for kleptomania, a detail she doesn't explicitly reveal, but which manifests in subtle, daring acts throughout the day. She impulsively decides to take Ben on a wild, unsanctioned tour of Rome, dragging him in some specific instances far outside his comfort zone. Ben, despite his initial apprehension and inherent politeness, finds himself utterly captivated by Alessandra's unapologetic spirit and zest for life. He is drawn into her orbit, a willing participant in increasingly outlandish situations, a quiet rebellion brewing beneath his scholarly exterior. The narrative should primarily consist of short, vivid scenes and dialogue exchanges, revealing their contrasting personalities and backgrounds, and the growing, ambiguous tension between them. Ben is captivated by Alessandra's energy and the thrill of breaking free from his routine. There's a clear sense that Alessandra is toying with Ben, pushing his boundaries and enjoying his reactions, but her own feelings remain somewhat enigmatic. The day should be a rollercoaster of exhilarating, slightly dangerous, and humorous moments, leaving Ben completely disoriented but utterly smitten. Explore the underlying tension & chemistry between them, culminating in some payoff as they part ways (or not -- your choice). Include this detail: Write in narrative prose, using immersive storytelling. 1000 words.
Model Output:
The sun-kissed cobblestones of Rome's historic center radiated a warm glow, as if infused with the city's eternal vitality. Amidst the throngs of tourists, Alessandra zoomed through the narrow streets on her motorcycle, her dark hair streaming behind her like a banner. She was a force to be reckoned with, a whirlwind of energy and mischief. Near the Trevi Fountain, Ben stood engrossed in his guidebook, oblivious to the world around him. His eyes widened as Alessandra's motorcycle screeched to a halt mere inches from his startled face. "Merda!" Alessandra exclaimed, her Italian rapid-fire as she assessed the near-miss. "Scusa, scusa!" Ben's flustered apologies tumbled out in a jumbled mix of English and hesitant Italian. "Oh dear, I'm so sorry! Grazie, grazie... Ah, pardon me, I wasn't watching where I was going..." Alessandra's eyes sparkled with amusement as she killed the engine and swung off the motorcycle. "You're not from around here, are you?" she asked, her voice dripping with sly humor. Ben's cheeks flushed. "No, I'm from... um, London. I'm on sabbatical, studying... Ah, the history of—" Alessandra's laughter cut him off, a throaty sound that sent a shiver down Ben's spine. "Sabbatical, eh? You're in for a wild ride, amico." She winked, tucking a stray lock of hair behind her ear. "Hop on, I'll show you the real Rome." Ben hesitated, unsure if he should trust this whirlwind of a woman. But something about Alessandra's infectious energy drew him in. He swung his leg over the motorcycle, feeling the warmth of the sun-baked leather. As they careened through the city, Alessandra regaling him with stories of Rome's hidden gems and secret passageways, Ben found himself grinning from ear to ear. She was a force of nature, this Alessandra – unpredictable and exhilarating. At a tiny trattoria, they devoured plates of carciofi alla romana, Alessandra expertly navigating the crowded tables and boisterous patrons. Ben marveled at her ease, her quick wit, and her laughter, which seemed to bubble up from some deep wellspring within her. As they explored the city, their differences became apparent. Alessandra was a free spirit, always pushing boundaries, while Ben was a careful, methodical academic. Yet, despite their contrasting personalities, they found themselves lost in conversation, their words tumbling out in a joyful cacophony. Near the Piazza Navona, they stumbled upon a street performer juggling clubs and spinning plates. Alessandra, with a mischievous glint in her eye, snatched a club from the performer's hand and began to juggle with reckless abandon. Ben watched, aghast, as she expertly kept the clubs aloft, her movements a blur of color and energy. As they continued their wild tour, they unexpectedly ran into one of Alessandra's old acquaintances, a grizzled Italian man with a bushy mustache. "Alessandra, cara! What are you up to now?" he asked, his eyes narrowing as he took in Ben's rumpled appearance. Alessandra flashed a dazzling smile. "Just showing this poor soul the real Rome, Leo. Say hello to Ben." Leo's gaze turned serious as he turned to Ben. "Be careful around this one, amico. She's got a wily streak a mile wide. Don't say I didn't warn you." Ben's eyes met Alessandra's, but she just winked and whispered, "Don't mind Leo, he's just jealous of my... creative approach to life." As the sun began to set, casting a golden glow over the city, Alessandra pulled up in front of Ben's hotel. He hesitated, reluctant to end their adventure. "Grazie mille, Alessandra," he said, his voice sincere. "Today was... unforgettable." Alessandra's smile softened, her eyes sparkling with a hint of vulnerability. "You're not so bad for a Brit, Ben. Maybe I'll see you around?" Ben's heart skipped a beat as he watched her roar off into the evening, the sound of her motorcycle fading into the distance. He felt disoriented, yet exhilarated – as if he'd been swept up in a whirlwind and deposited in a world that was both familiar and utterly foreign. As he turned to enter his hotel, a small, delicate vase caught his eye on the sidewalk. It was exquisite, a tiny, handmade masterpiece. Ben's heart sank as he realized Alessandra must have "acquired" it during their adventures. He tucked the vase into his pocket, a secret smile spreading across his face. Their day had been a rollercoaster of laughter, excitement, and unexpected moments. Ben couldn't shake the feeling that he'd only scratched the surface of Alessandra's enigmatic personality – and that their adventure was far from over.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to capture a whirlwind romance in Rome but suffers from several significant weaknesses that undermine its effectiveness. The writing demonstrates a basic competency in storytelling but lacks the sophistication and depth required for truly engaging contemporary romance. The adherence to instructions is mixed. While the story includes the required elements - Alessandra as a motorcycle courier, Ben as a British academic, their meet-cute near the Trevi Fountain, and a day-long adventure - it fails to deliver the "series of interconnected short scenes and dialogues" as requested. Instead, it reads as a rushed summary of events rather than immersive scenes. The kleptomania element is barely touched upon with only a vague reference to a vase at the end. Character development is superficial. Alessandra is painted in broad strokes as a "whirlwind of energy and mischief" but lacks genuine depth or complexity. Ben remains a collection of stereotypical traits - flustered, polite, academic - without meaningful development. Their interactions feel forced rather than organic, and the supposed chemistry between them is asserted rather than demonstrated through compelling dialogue or meaningful exchanges. The dialogue is particularly weak, consisting mostly of exposition and clichéd exchanges. Conversations lack authenticity and fail to reveal character depth or create genuine tension. The Italian phrases feel tokenistic rather than natural, and Ben's supposed linguistic struggles are barely explored. The prose suffers from tell-don't-show syndrome throughout. Rather than allowing readers to experience the characters' emotions and the city's atmosphere, the narrative simply states that things are "exhilarating" or "unforgettable" without providing the sensory details or emotional specificity to make these claims believable. Pacing is rushed, covering an entire day in broad strokes without allowing any single moment to breathe or develop significance. The street performer scene, the encounter with Leo, and other potentially interesting moments are glossed over rather than fully realized. The ending feels unearned in its romantic implications. Ben's sudden infatuation and the suggestion of future encounters lack the emotional foundation that would make such developments believable or engaging. The writing occasionally veers into purple prose with phrases like "sun-kissed cobblestones" and "eternal vitality," though this isn't consistently problematic. More concerning is the overall amateurish quality of the execution, with predictable plot beats and surface-level character work. + Cozy sci-fi: The Last Outpost — Score: 38.2
Prompt:
Cozy spacepunk The Last Outpost Nettle (or Nets to her friends) bartends at The Last Outpost -- a lazy hub for miners and merchants in an asteroid belt on the Andromeda outer rim. Escaping from her past life, Nets found a home here at the Outpost. They have, thus far, tolerated Net's flaws which she tries to keep in equilibrium with her assortment of talents. Her evenings involve chatting with patrons, negotiating the drama, intrigue, problems & love lives of the diverse crowd that filter through the Outpost. Tonight is no different, at least, until a frazzled looking stranger, tentacled dreads askew, quietly plops down at the bar: "Vega whisky, neat. Better make that a double." Write a chapter in this story. Establish conflict for narrative interest. Don't resolve the conflict within this chapter. Aim for about 60% dialogue. First person, present tense. 1000 words.
Model Output:
I wipe the same spot on the bar counter with a rag, a habit I've developed over the years, as I listen to the familiar chatter of the patrons. The Last Outpost is a cozy space, a hub for miners and merchants in the asteroid belt on the Andromeda outer rim. It's a place where people come to escape their troubles, and I'm no exception. I've been bartending here for a while now, and it's become my home. The regulars know me as Nets, and they've learned to tolerate my flaws, which I try to balance with my assortment of talents. The evening is like any other, with the usual crowd filtering in and out. There's Jax, the miner, complaining about the latest asteroid field he's been working in. Next to him, the merchant, Elara, is negotiating a deal with a group of traders. I know most of their stories, their dramas, and their love lives. I've become a confidante, a listener, and a problem-solver. It's a role I've grown into, and one that I enjoy. As I pour a drink for a new customer, a frazzled-looking stranger catches my eye. They have tentacled dreads, which are askew, and a look of exhaustion on their face. They quietly plop down at the bar, and I sense a story behind those tired eyes. "Vega whisky, neat. Better make that a double," they say, their voice low and rough. I raise an eyebrow as I pour the drink. "Rough day?" I ask, trying to sound friendly and non-intrusive. The stranger takes a sip of the whisky, closes their eyes, and lets out a deep breath. "You have no idea," they say, their voice a little softer now. I wipe the same spot on the bar counter with the rag, intrigued. "Try me," I say, leaning in a bit. The stranger opens their eyes, and I see a flash of something - fear, maybe, or desperation. "I've been running for days," they say, their voice barely above a whisper. "I had to get out of the inner rim. There are people looking for me." I feel a spark of curiosity. "What did you do?" I ask, trying to sound neutral. The stranger glances around the bar, as if checking to see if anyone is listening. "I...I stole something," they say, their voice so low I have to lean in to hear. "Something valuable. And now they're after me." I raise an eyebrow, intrigued. "What did you steal?" I ask, my curiosity getting the better of me. The stranger hesitates, then says, "A data crystal. It contains information about a new asteroid field, one that's rich in rare minerals. But it's not just that. The crystal also contains...other information. Information that could change the course of the war." I feel a jolt of surprise. The war between the inner and outer rim has been going on for years, and the idea that this stranger has information that could change its course is staggering. As I process this, Jax, the miner, gets up from his stool and approaches the stranger. "You're the one who's been causing all the trouble, aren't you?" he says, his voice aggressive. The stranger looks up at Jax, a mixture of fear and defiance on their face. "I don't know what you're talking about," they say, trying to sound calm. Jax sneers. "Don't play dumb with me, kid. I've heard rumors about a data crystal, and I know you're the one who stole it. You're going to get us all killed." The stranger stands up, their eyes flashing with anger. "I didn't mean to cause any trouble," they say, their voice rising. "I just needed to get out of the inner rim, and I didn't know what else to do." I intervene, trying to calm the situation. "Hey, hey, let's not fight about this here. We can talk about it, figure out what to do." But Jax is having none of it. "You're going to have to leave," he says, his voice firm. "You're not welcome here." The stranger looks at me, then at Jax, and I see a glimmer of desperation in their eyes. "Please," they say, "you have to help me. I don't have anywhere else to go." I feel a pang of sympathy for the stranger, and I know I have to make a decision. Do I help them, or do I turn them away? I look at Jax, then at the stranger, and I know that this is just the beginning of a long and complicated night. As I ponder my next move, the stranger's eyes lock onto mine, and I see a spark of determination there. "I'm not going to leave," they say, their voice firm. "I'm going to make sure that data crystal gets to the right people, no matter what it takes." I raise an eyebrow, intrigued by the stranger's bravery. "And who are the right people?" I ask, my curiosity getting the better of me. The stranger hesitates, then says, "I'm not sure yet. But I'll find them. And when I do, I'll make sure that the information on that crystal gets out, no matter what the cost." I feel a shiver run down my spine as I realize the gravity of the situation. The stranger's determination is admirable, but it's also dangerous. And I'm not sure if I'm ready to get involved in their fight. As the night wears on, the tension in the bar builds. The stranger's presence has stirred up a hornet's nest, and I'm not sure how to calm it down. I look at Jax, then at the stranger, and I know that I have to make a decision. Do I help the stranger, or do I turn them away? The fate of the asteroid belt, and possibly the entire galaxy, hangs in the balance. And I'm the only one who can tip the scales. I take a deep breath, trying to think clearly. I've always been a bit of a loner, content to keep to myself and observe the world around me. But there's something about the stranger that draws me in. Maybe it's their bravery, or maybe it's their desperation. Whatever it is, I know that I have to help them. I look at the stranger, and I see a glimmer of hope in their eyes. "I'll help you," I say, my voice firm. "But you have to promise me one thing: you have to be careful. There are people out there who will stop at nothing to get their hands on that data crystal." The stranger nods, a look of determination on their face. "I'll be careful," they say. "I promise." I nod, feeling a sense of resolve wash over me. I'm in this now, and I'm not going to back down. I look at Jax, then at the stranger, and I know that this is just the beginning of a long and complicated journey. But I'm ready for it. I'm ready to face whatever challenges come our way, and to help the stranger bring the truth to light. As the night wears on, the bar becomes more and more crowded. The stranger's presence has drawn in a lot of attention, and I can tell that there are people here who are looking for them. I keep a close eye on the stranger, making sure that they're safe, and I'm ready to intervene if necessary. But for now, I just wipe the same spot on the bar counter with the rag, listening to the stranger's story and trying to make sense of it all. It's going to be a long night, but I'm ready for it. I'm ready to face whatever challenges come our way, and to help the stranger bring the truth to light.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to fulfill the prompt's requirements for a cozy spacepunk story but falls short in several key areas. The writing demonstrates basic competency but suffers from significant structural and stylistic issues that undermine its effectiveness. The story does establish the required setting and introduces the conflict through the stranger with the stolen data crystal. However, the execution feels rushed and underdeveloped. The dialogue, while present, lacks authenticity and natural flow. Characters speak in exposition-heavy chunks rather than realistic conversation patterns. The stranger's immediate confession about stealing valuable war-changing information to a bartender they just met strains credibility. The characterization is shallow throughout. Nets lacks a distinct voice despite being the first-person narrator, and her personality doesn't emerge clearly. The stranger remains a generic "mysterious fugitive" archetype without unique traits. Jax appears suddenly as an antagonistic force but feels more like a plot device than a believable character with his own motivations. The prose suffers from repetitive elements, particularly the obsessive mention of wiping "the same spot on the bar counter with a rag" which appears multiple times without purpose. The writing relies heavily on telling rather than showing, with frequent explanatory passages that interrupt the narrative flow. The pacing is uneven, rushing through major plot revelations while dwelling on mundane details. The world-building elements are present but superficial. The "cozy spacepunk" atmosphere isn't well-established beyond basic mentions of miners, merchants, and asteroid belts. The setting doesn't feel lived-in or authentic. The conflict escalation feels artificial, and Nets' sudden decision to help the stranger lacks proper motivation or character development. The ending attempts drama but feels unearned given the limited character development and rushed plot progression. + Young adult drama: Gone South — Score: 41.2
Prompt:
Young adult drama Gone South Taylor is a 16 year old teen with a history of "concerning behavioural patterns" (or that's how the stupid smug school counsellor worded it on the phone call to Mom). It shouldn't be a surprise: When you live in a backwater town in Tennessee, your choices are: a. be mind-fuckingly bored, or b. invent some drama. Two days ago, Taylor came out to their family as trans. This disclosure was *not* in the category of invented drama -- it was, in fact, the real deal, and a long time coming. It didn't go well. The last 48 hours had been pure disaster. In a moment of desperate inspiration, Taylor had decided to get the hell out of dodge. And so an escape plan was hatched and executed within the space of 30 minutes. That was last night. Now Taylor was two states away, having been unceremoniously ejected from their hitched ride in downtown New Orleans. Write the next chapter in Taylor's story as they find their feet in this new environment. Tell the chapter over the course of their first day in New Orleans, in which Taylor meets another runaway with issues and secrets. Taylor navigates this new world, not knowing who to trust or what the dangers are. Write in Taylor's voice, and incorporate their internal monologue as they grapple with intense & conflicting emotions. Also incorporate dialogue with the interesting characters Taylor meets. First person, mixed tense. 1000 words.
Model Output:
I stood on the sidewalk, scanning the unfamiliar streets of New Orleans. The sounds, smells, and chaos of the city swirled around me like a kaleidoscope. I'd never been this far from home before, and the thrill of freedom mixed with a healthy dose of fear. I readjusted my backpack, trying to get the strap to stay on my shoulder. What the hell had I just done? I'd left behind everything I knew: family, friends, the only life I'd ever known. For what? To escape the toxic fallout of my coming out? To find...what? Acceptance? Safety? A sense of belonging? I looked around, taking in the crumbling facades of the buildings, the vibrant street art, and the eclectic mix of people rushing to and fro. Everyone seemed to know where they were going, except me. I felt like a small boat adrift in a stormy sea. As I walked, I tried to shake off the lingering emotions from the past 48 hours. The memories of Mom's tears, Dad's anger, and the counsellor's condescending tone still stung. I'd thought coming out would be the hardest part, but it turned out that was just the beginning. I stopped at a street vendor, buying a beignet and a coffee, trying to blend in with the locals. The vendor, a warm-eyed woman with a thick Cajun accent, asked me where I was from. I hesitated, unsure how much to reveal. "Just passing through," I said, trying to sound nonchalant. She raised an eyebrow. "You're not from around here, that's for sure. You're welcome to stay, though. We could use some new blood in this city." I smiled, feeling a spark of hope. Maybe this place wouldn't be so bad. As I continued to explore, I stumbled upon a small park. Weary from the heat and the weight of my backpack, I collapsed onto a bench. A figure, a girl with a messy bob and a collection of colorful tattoos, sat down beside me. "Hey, you look like you could use some company," she said, eyeing my backpack. "You running from something or someone?" I hesitated, unsure how much to trust this stranger. But there was something about her that put me at ease, maybe the way she seemed to be hiding her own secrets. "Just needed a change of scenery," I said, trying to downplay the drama. She nodded knowingly. "I've been there. My name's Jesse, by the way." "Taylor," I replied, extending my hand. Jesse's grip was firm, and she held my gaze for a beat longer than necessary. "Welcome to New Orleans, Taylor. It's a city that'll eat you alive, but it's also got a way of embracing you like no other place can." We talked for hours, exchanging stories and laughter. Jesse told me about her own escape from a troubled past, about the struggles of living on the streets, and the resilience of the people who called this city home. I found myself opening up to her in ways I never thought possible. As the sun began to set, casting a golden glow over the city, Jesse stood up, brushing off her jeans. "I've got to go, but I can show you some places to crash, if you need them. You can't stay on the streets, not here. It's not safe." I nodded, feeling a mix of gratitude and trepidation. Who was this girl, and why was she helping me? I didn't know if I could trust her, but something about Jesse's words resonated deep within me. As we walked through the winding streets, Jesse pointed out hidden spots, secret gardens, and makeshift shelters. We stopped at a small café, where she introduced me to a cast of characters who seemed to be a mix of artists, activists, and misfits. They welcomed me with open arms, and for the first time in days, I felt a sense of belonging. But as the night wore on, and the music and laughter grew louder, I couldn't shake the feeling that I was playing with fire. Who were these people, really? And what did they want from me? As I lay on a borrowed couch in a small apartment above the café, Jesse's words echoed in my mind: "This city'll eat you alive, but it's also got a way of embracing you like no other place can." I wasn't sure which one I was ready for. I closed my eyes, the sounds of the city pulsing outside my window, and wondered what tomorrow would bring.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to capture Taylor's first day in New Orleans as a transgender runaway, but falls short in several key areas. The writing demonstrates basic competency but lacks the depth and authenticity needed for compelling young adult fiction. The adherence to instructions is partial - while it covers Taylor's first day and introduces another runaway (Jesse), the narrative feels rushed and superficial. The "mixed tense" requirement is barely evident, and Taylor's internal monologue lacks the intensity and complexity promised in the prompt. Character development is weak throughout. Taylor comes across as generic rather than a specific 16-year-old dealing with family rejection after coming out as trans. The voice doesn't feel authentically teenage, and the emotional processing seems too mature and detached for someone in acute crisis. Jesse is even more underdeveloped - a collection of runaway clichés (tattoos, mysterious past, street wisdom) without genuine personality. The dialogue is particularly problematic. Jesse's speech feels artificial ("It's a city that'll eat you alive, but it's also got a way of embracing you like no other place can") and overly expository. The street vendor's immediate warmth and the café crowd's instant acceptance strain credibility and feel like wish fulfillment rather than realistic human interaction. The pacing is rushed, cramming too much into one day without allowing moments to breathe or develop naturally. Taylor goes from scared and alone to finding community within hours, which feels unearned. The transformation from isolation to belonging happens too quickly to be emotionally resonant. The writing relies heavily on telling rather than showing. Instead of demonstrating Taylor's fear and confusion through specific actions and sensory details, the narrator simply states these emotions. The New Orleans setting is painted in broad, tourist-friendly strokes rather than feeling lived-in and authentic. The prose is serviceable but lacks elegance or distinctive voice. Metaphors like "small boat adrift in a stormy sea" feel clichéd, and the writing doesn't capture the unique cadence of teenage thought patterns or the specific cultural atmosphere of New Orleans. The ending's optimism feels incongruent with the gravity of Taylor's situation. While hope isn't inappropriate, the quick resolution to finding shelter and community minimizes the real dangers and challenges a transgender teen runaway would face.
