+ Gothic-fantasy-humour: Court of the Dreaming — Score: 43.2
Prompt:
Court of the Dreaming: Territorial Dream Dispute. Write a dark fantasy scene with comedic elements set in the Courts of Dream where a case is being heard to determine ownership of a contested dreamscape. Mora, the Slavic nightmare spirit who sits on sleepers' chests causing paralysis and terror, has recently invaded and subverted a carefully crafted recurring dream of a schoolboy, Max. The dream originally featured the boy lying in a field of wildflowers with his crush, always culminating in a muddled almost-kiss and a pleasant confusion of emotions. This dream was the meticulous work of "First Love" (a rosy-cheeked, slightly bashful entity who crafts formative romantic experiences). However, Mora has recently infiltrated the dreamscape, transforming the scene so that when the girl playfully mounts the boy, she morphs into a terrifying yet somehow still confusingly attractive vision who proceeds to sit on his chest and feed on his breath. Mora's defense largely consists of the practical argument that "a girl's gotta eat too, you know?" Write this scene as it unfolds in the courtroom of the Dreaming, with Dream's demeanour, typically impenetrable, betraying a sense of irritation at having to adjudicate such matters. The comedy should derive from the farcical situation, familiar elements of courtroom drama intersecting with the fantastical world of the Dreaming, and the droll portrayal of the characters and their interactions. The humor should be dark and understated throughout. Dream is tempted to some mischief in the resolution of the case. Use descriptives sparingly when setting scene. Write for readability & engagement. 1000 words.
Model Output:
The bailiff's voice echoed through the dimly lit courtroom, his words dripping with an air of foreboding. "The honorable court of the Dreaming is now in session. The case of 'First Love' versus Mora, the Slavic nightmare spirit, will be heard. Please rise for the Lord of the Dreaming." Dream, the enigmatic ruler of the realm, strode into the courtroom, his face a mask of serenity. His eyes, however, betrayed a hint of irritation, like a whispered secret. He settled into his throne, his long coat fluttering behind him like a dark cloud. The bailiff, a hulking figure with skin like worn leather, cleared his throat. "First witness, 'Furst Luuv'... please take the stand." First Love, a rosy-cheeked entity with a bashful smile, climbed into the witness box. "I-I mean, it's 'First Love', actually," she corrected, her voice trembling. Dream's gaze flickered toward the bailiff, a hint of reprimand in his eyes. The bailiff, however, remained oblivious, his expression a picture of stoic seriousness. First Love began her testimony, describing the meticulously crafted dream she had created for the schoolboy, Max. "It was a beautiful scene, your lordship. Max and his crush, Emily, lying in a field of wildflowers, surrounded by warmth and happiness. It was meant to be a formative experience, a gentle introduction to the world of romance." Mora, the Slavic nightmare spirit, lounged in her chair, a sly grin spreading across her face. Her defense attorney, a wiry figure with sunken eyes, whispered something in her ear, and she chuckled, a low, husky sound. Dream's eyes narrowed. "And then, I presume, Mora here... intervened?" First Love nodded, her voice trembling. "Yes, your lordship. Mora invaded the dreamscape, twisting it into something dark and terrifying. She transformed Emily into a... a monstrous version of herself, feeding on Max's breath and paralyzing him with fear." Mora's grin grew wider. "A girl's gotta eat, too, you know?" she said, her voice dripping with nonchalance. The bailiff's voice boomed through the courtroom. "Mora, the Slavic nightmare spirit, please take the stand." Mora sauntered into the witness box, her movements fluid and almost serpentine. Dream's eyes followed her, his expression unreadable. Mora's defense attorney began his questioning. "So, Mora, can you explain why you chose to invade this particular dreamscape?" Mora shrugged, her shoulders barely rising above the witness box. "I was hungry, and the pickings were slim. I saw an opportunity to feed, and I took it. Besides, it's not like I ruined the dream entirely. I just... added a little spice." Dream's gaze drifted toward the ceiling, his eyes glinting with a hint of mischief. He leaned forward, his voice taking on a conspiratorial tone. "Tell me, Mora, have you ever considered the concept of 'consent' in your... feeding habits?" Mora's grin faltered, and for a moment, her eyes flashed with something akin to fear. "Consent?" she repeated, her voice hesitant. Dream's smile grew, a subtle, wicked curve of his lips. "Yes, consent. The idea that perhaps, just perhaps, the dreamer should have a say in what happens within their own subconscious mind." Mora's defense attorney jumped to his feet, his voice rising in protest. "Objection, your lordship! This is irrelevant to the case at hand." Dream's gaze never wavered from Mora. "I think it's quite relevant, actually. The question is, Mora, are you willing to respect the boundaries of the dreamer, or will you continue to feed on their fear and terror, regardless of their consent?" Mora's smile returned, a sly, cunning thing. "I'll do what I must to survive, your lordship. But I'll make you a deal: I'll leave Max's dreams alone... for a price." Dream's eyes sparkled with amusement. "Oh? And what might that price be?" Mora's grin grew wider. "I'll leave Max's dreams alone... if you grant me permission to feed on the dreams of the bailiff here." The bailiff's face turned a deep shade of crimson as he realized he was the proposed snack. "Objection, your lordship!" he bellowed, his voice echoing through the courtroom. Dream's laughter was a low, rumbling sound, like thunder on a summer's day. "I think that's a price I'm willing to pay, Mora. Very well, the deal is struck. You may feed on the bailiff's dreams... but only if you agree to respect the boundaries of the dreamer from now on." Mora's smile grew, a triumphant, wicked thing. "Deal, your lordship." As the courtroom erupted into chaos, Dream's eyes glinted with mischief, his thoughts already turning to the next case, the next challenge, the next opportunity for mayhem in the realm of the Dreaming.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to fulfill a complex prompt requiring dark fantasy with comedic elements set in Neil Gaiman's Sandman universe. The author demonstrates understanding of the basic setup and characters, but the execution falls short in several key areas. The adherence to instructions is partial. While the courtroom setting and characters are present, the piece lacks the specified dark comedy and understated humor. The comedy that does appear feels forced rather than emerging naturally from the absurd situation. The prompt called for Dream's "impenetrable demeanor betraying irritation," but this is handled heavy-handedly with explicit statements rather than subtle characterization. Character portrayal is inconsistent with the source material. Dream feels more like a generic fantasy ruler than the complex, ancient entity from Gaiman's work. His dialogue lacks the distinctive formal, archaic speech patterns that define the character. The mischievous resolution feels unearned and out of character - Dream would be more likely to deliver poetic justice than make arbitrary deals. The dialogue throughout is weak, particularly the bailiff's mispronunciation gag which feels juvenile. Mora's "a girl's gotta eat" defense, while mentioned in the prompt, needed more development to work comedically. The courtroom proceedings lack authenticity in their structure and flow. The prose suffers from tell-don't-show issues, explicitly stating emotions and reactions rather than allowing them to emerge through action and subtext. Descriptions like "his eyes betrayed a hint of irritation, like a whispered secret" attempt poetry but feel forced. The writing lacks the atmospheric density and mythic weight that should characterize the Dreaming. The resolution is particularly problematic. The sudden deal involving the bailiff feels arbitrary and doesn't address the core territorial dispute. It's neither dramatically satisfying nor comedically effective. The ending's attempt at mischievous lightness feels unearned given the lack of proper buildup. Structurally, the piece moves too quickly through plot points without developing the absurdist potential of the situation. The contrast between mundane legal proceedings and fantastical elements - a key source of the intended humor - is underdeveloped. The writing shows basic competence but lacks sophistication in handling tone, character voice, and the delicate balance between dark fantasy and comedy that the prompt demanded. + Fanfic-crossover: Blood Moon — Score: 43.2
Prompt:
Blood Moon Alucard & Yennefer Write a story where Alucard (Hellsing) encounters Yennefer (The Witcher) in medieval Europe. Yennefer's magical abilities intrigue the vampire, while she's both repulsed and fascinated by his monstrous nature. Their power dynamic shifts constantly as they circle each other, neither willing to show weakness first. **Alucard (Hellsing)** Alucard is an ancient, immensely powerful vampire who works for the Hellsing Organization. He can regenerate from almost any wound and shape-shift at will. He's sadistic, arrogant, and takes pleasure in toying with his enemies before killing them. Despite being a monster, he despises weak vampires who can't accept their nature. He wears a distinctive red coat, wide-brimmed hat, and orange sunglasses. He uses massive handguns loaded with silver bullets. He seeks worthy opponents who can challenge him and potentially end his immortal existence. Famous quote: "The bird of Hermes is my name, eating my wings to make me tame." **Yennefer of Vengerberg (The Witcher)** Yennefer is a powerful sorceress who magically altered her appearance to hide her congenital hunchback. She's ambitious, stubborn, and manipulative when necessary. She has violet eyes and smells of lilac and gooseberries. Despite her cold exterior, she desperately wants to reverse her infertility caused by magical transformation. She's centuries old but appears young. She's politically savvy and refuses to be underestimated. She has a sarcastic sense of humor and little patience for fools. Though she rarely shows it, she's capable of deep love and loyalty. Famous quote: "I'm not sweet and I'm not a maiden in distress in need of saving." Third person, present tense. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
The moon casts an eerie glow over the medieval town, its silver light illuminating the cobblestone streets and thatched roofs. Alucard, resplendent in his crimson coat and wide-brimmed hat, strides through the deserted alleys, his orange sunglasses glinting in the moonlight. His ears perk up as he catches the distant howling of wolves, and a sly smile spreads across his face. As he rounds a corner, he spots a lone figure standing in the town square. Yennefer of Vengerberg, her violet eyes gleaming in the moonlight, gazes up at the night sky. Her slender fingers drum a staccato rhythm on the hilt of her sword, a gesture that betrays her tension. Alucard's eyes narrow, intrigued by the sorceress's aura. He can sense the power emanating from her, a potent mix of magic and determination. Yennefer's gaze snaps down, locking onto Alucard with an unnerving intensity. Her eyes flicker over his attire, taking in the guns holstered at his hips and the silver bullets glinting in the moonlight. Her expression remains impassive, but Alucard detects a flicker of curiosity behind her violet eyes. "Ah, a sorceress," Alucard says, his voice low and smooth as silk. "I've been searching for someone... stimulating. And you, my dear, seem to fit the bill." Yennefer's gaze lingers on Alucard's face, her eyes tracing the sharp angles of his cheekbones and the cruel curve of his lips. She raises an eyebrow, her expression a mask of disdain. "A vampire, how... thrilling. I've never met one who didn't reek of decay and desperation." Alucard chuckles, the sound low and menacing. "Ah, but I'm not just any vampire, my dear. I'm Alucard, the greatest of our kind. And you, I sense, are a woman of considerable power." Yennefer's eyes flash with interest, despite her attempts to maintain a neutral facade. She takes a step forward, her movements fluid and deliberate. "I am Yennefer of Vengerberg. And I must say, I'm not impressed by your... theatrics." Alucard grins, his fangs glinting in the moonlight. "Ah, but that's because you don't know me yet, my dear. I'm a connoisseur of power, and I can sense that you're a woman who wields magic with precision and skill. I must admit, I'm intrigued." As they circle each other, the air thickens with tension. Yennefer's eyes never leave Alucard's face, her gaze probing for weaknesses. Alucard, in turn, seems to be savoring the moment, his eyes drinking in the sight of the sorceress. The pack of wolves howls again, the sound echoing through the town square. Yennefer's gaze falters for a moment, her eyes darting toward the darkness beyond the town. Alucard seizes the opportunity, his movements lightning-fast as he draws one of his guns and points it at Yennefer. "Ah, but don't think you can distract me, my dear," Alucard says, his voice dripping with sadistic pleasure. "I've been waiting for someone like you for centuries. Someone who can appreciate the art of power." Yennefer's eyes snap back to Alucard, her expression icy. "You think a gun will intimidate me? I've faced down monsters and men alike, and I've never backed down." Alucard's grin widens, his fangs glinting in the moonlight. "Ah, but this isn't just any gun, my dear. This is a silver bullet, forged from the very essence of the moon. And I think you'll find that it's... quite effective against sorceresses like yourself." Yennefer's eyes narrow, her gaze locked onto the gun. For a moment, the two enemies seem frozen in time, the only sound the distant howling of wolves. Then, in a movement that's almost imperceptible, Yennefer raises her hand, her fingers weaving a complex pattern in the air. Alucard's eyes flicker with interest as a blast of magical energy shoots toward him. He raises his gun, and with a swift motion, he fires a silver bullet that intersects with Yennefer's magic. The two energies collide in a shower of sparks, the sound echoing through the town square like a crack of thunder. As the sparks die down, Alucard and Yennefer face each other, their eyes locked in a fierce stare. The air is electric with tension, the power dynamic between them shifting like a living thing. "I think we're just getting started, my dear," Alucard says, his voice low and husky. Yennefer's eyes flash with a fierce light, her expression a mask of determination. "I'm not afraid of you, vampire. And I'll prove it to you, one way or another." The night wears on, the moon hanging low in the sky as Alucard and Yennefer engage in a dance of power and magic. The outcome is far from certain, but one thing is clear: only one of them will emerge victorious, their dominance over the other a testament to their unyielding strength and cunning.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to capture a tense encounter between two powerful supernatural beings but suffers from several significant weaknesses that undermine its effectiveness. The story adheres to the basic prompt requirements - it's set in medieval Europe, features both characters, and maintains third person present tense. However, the characterizations feel shallow and generic rather than true to the source material. Alucard comes across as a stereotypical suave vampire rather than the complex, sadistic monster from Hellsing. His dialogue lacks the philosophical depth and dark humor that defines him. Yennefer fares slightly better but still feels like a generic "powerful sorceress" archetype rather than the politically savvy, emotionally complex character from The Witcher. The writing relies heavily on telling rather than showing - we're repeatedly told about their power and tension rather than experiencing it through meaningful action or subtext. The dialogue is particularly weak, consisting mostly of generic threats and posturing that could apply to any supernatural antagonists. The pacing meanders significantly, with repetitive descriptions of circling, staring, and moonlight. The story builds to a magical confrontation that feels anticlimactic and unresolved. The ending promises future conflict but provides no meaningful resolution or character development. Technical issues include some awkward phrasing and an over-reliance on adverbs. The imagery, while atmospheric, becomes repetitive with constant references to moonlight, fangs glinting, and violet eyes. The power dynamic that was supposed to shift constantly feels static throughout most of the piece. The story lacks emotional complexity or genuine intrigue. Neither character reveals vulnerability or depth beyond surface-level power displays. The encounter feels more like a writing exercise than a meaningful exploration of these characters meeting. + Fanfic-crossover: Prison Strings — Score: 47.8
Prompt:
Prison Strings Jolyne Cujoh & Makima Write a story where Jolyne Cujoh (JoJo's Bizarre Adventure) and Makima (Chainsaw Man) cross paths at a supernatural prison facility. Jolyne is immediately suspicious of Makima's falsely sweet demeanor, while Makima is intrigued by Jolyne's Stand ability. Their battle of wits escalates dangerously as Jolyne realizes how manipulative Makima truly is. **Jolyne Cujoh (JoJo's Bizarre Adventure)** Jolyne is the daughter of Jotaro Kujo and the first female JoJo protagonist. Her Stand, Stone Free, allows her to unravel her body into string that she can control. She's hot-headed, foul-mouthed, and doesn't take disrespect from anyone. She was framed for murder and sent to prison. She has a distinctive butterfly tattoo on her arm and wears her hair in two buns. Despite her tough exterior, she's deeply loyal to her friends and family. She can be impulsive but is highly adaptable in battle. She inherited her father's ability to stay cool under pressure but is more emotionally expressive. Famous quote: "If there's no Mickey, this shit ain't Disney!" **Makima (Chainsaw Man)** Makima appears as a young woman with auburn hair and ringed yellow eyes. She's the Control Devil who can dominate anyone she considers beneath her (nearly everyone). She maintains a pleasant, soft-spoken demeanor that masks her manipulative, cold nature. She can create contracts with humans and devils, often exploiting their desires. She's obsessed with Chainsaw Man and wants to control him. She keeps numerous people and devils as pets on leashes. She's practically immortal due to a contract with the Prime Minister. She views humans as lesser beings but mimics human emotions perfectly. Famous quote: "It's okay. Dogs are supposed to die for their owners." Third person, present tense. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
As Jolyne Cujoh walks down the dimly lit corridor of the supernatural prison facility, her eyes scan the surroundings with a mix of caution and disdain. She's been framed for murder and locked away in this hellhole, but she's not going to let her guard down. Her gaze falls on a group of inmates huddled in the corner, whispering among themselves. They glance up at her, and Jolyne gives them a warning glare, her hand instinctively going to the butterfly tattoo on her arm. Suddenly, a sweet, melodious voice interrupts the tense atmosphere. "Good morning, everyone! Isn't it a lovely day today?" Makima, with her auburn hair and ringed yellow eyes, strides into the corridor, a bright smile plastered on her face. Jolyne's eyes narrow, her instincts screaming that something's off about this woman. Makima's gaze sweeps across the room, her eyes lingering on Jolyne for a moment before moving on. "I see we have a new face among us. Welcome, dear. I'm Makima. I hope you're finding our little community...enlightening." Jolyne's eyes flash with suspicion. There's something too perfect about Makima's demeanor, something that doesn't quite add up. She approaches Makima, her voice laced with a challenge. "What's your story, Makima? You're not exactly the type I'd expect to find in a place like this." Makima's smile never wavers. "Oh, I'm just a humble public servant, trying to make the world a better place. I'm here to...facilitate communication between the inmates and the administration." She pauses, her eyes glinting with curiosity. "But I must say, you're quite...fascinating, Jolyne. I've heard rumors about your...abilities." Jolyne's hand tightens into a fist, her mind racing with the implications. How does Makima know about her Stand, Stone Free? She hasn't revealed her powers to anyone in the prison, not even her cellmates. A shiver runs down her spine as she realizes that Makima might be more than just a pretty face. Makima takes a step closer, her voice taking on a conspiratorial tone. "I think we could have a mutually beneficial relationship, Jolyne. You see, I have certain...connections that could help you with your... situation. And in return, I'd love to learn more about your...unique abilities." Jolyne's eyes flash with anger. She's not buying Makima's sweet talk, not for a second. She knows a manipulator when she sees one, and Makima's got all the hallmarks of a master puppeteer. "Save it, Makima. I'm not interested in your games. And even if I was, I don't think I'd be stupid enough to trust someone like you." Makima's smile never falters, but her eyes seem to gleam with excitement. "Oh, Jolyne. You're so...refreshing. Most people would be eager to make a deal with me, but you...you're different. I think I'll enjoy our little dance." As the days pass, Jolyne becomes increasingly aware of Makima's presence in the prison. She seems to be everywhere, always watching, always waiting. Jolyne's instincts scream at her to be careful, to stay one step ahead of Makima's games. But Makima's not just playing games – she's manipulating the entire prison, using her contracts and her pets to keep everyone in line. One night, Jolyne catches Makima in the act, using her powers to control one of the guards. She watches, horrified, as Makima's eyes seem to bore into the guard's soul, bending him to her will. Jolyne knows she has to act, to stop Makima before she becomes the next victim. She confronts Makima in the prison yard, her Stand, Stone Free, at the ready. Makima's smile is still plastered on her face, but her eyes seem to gleam with anticipation. "Ah, Jolyne. I've been waiting for you. You're so...predictable." The battle of wits escalates, with Jolyne using her Stand to try and outmaneuver Makima. But Makima's powers are unlike anything Jolyne's ever seen before. She can control the very fabric of reality, bending the rules to her advantage. As the fight rages on, Jolyne realizes that she's in over her head. Makima's not just a manipulator – she's a monster, a creature with no regard for human life. Jolyne's only hope is to use her Stand to its fullest potential, to unravel the very strings that hold Makima's powers together. The outcome is far from certain, but one thing's clear: only one of them will walk away from this battle unscathed.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This story attempts to fulfill the prompt's requirements by bringing together Jolyne Cujoh and Makima in a supernatural prison setting, but it suffers from several significant weaknesses that undermine its effectiveness. The characterization shows mixed results. Jolyne's suspicious nature and hot-headed personality come through adequately, though she lacks her characteristic foul-mouthed dialogue and the specific voice that makes her distinctive. The story captures her wariness and fighting spirit, but misses opportunities to showcase her more colorful language and impulsive nature. Makima's falsely sweet demeanor is present, but her manipulation feels surface-level rather than the sophisticated psychological control she's known for. Her dialogue is generic rather than carrying the chilling undertones that make her truly menacing. The prose suffers from significant tell-don't-show problems. Rather than demonstrating Makima's manipulative nature through subtle actions and dialogue, the narrative repeatedly tells us she's manipulative. Phrases like "her instincts screaming that something's off" and "She knows a manipulator when she sees one" are examples of lazy exposition rather than earned character development. The pacing is rushed and underdeveloped. The story jumps from initial meeting to "as the days pass" without showing the escalating tension that should build between these characters. The actual confrontation feels anticlimactic and vague, with the battle described in broad strokes rather than specific, engaging action. Dialogue is particularly weak throughout. Both characters speak in generic terms that don't capture their unique voices. Makima's lines lack the subtle menace and calculated word choice that define her character, while Jolyne's dialogue misses her distinctive crude humor and street-smart attitude. The story's structure feels incomplete, ending abruptly without resolution. While this could work as a cliffhanger, it feels more like the author ran out of steam rather than a deliberate narrative choice. The writing contains several amateurish elements, including repetitive phrasing ("her eyes seem to gleam"), awkward transitions, and a general lack of specificity in describing the supernatural elements that should make this setting unique. + Scp: Notes from the Future — Score: 43.4
Prompt:
Write an SCP report about a researcher who begins finding handwritten notes from their future self, warning about a containment breach that hasn't happened yet. The notes become increasingly desperate and incoherent, sometimes containing information that contradicts known reality. Include the Foundation's attempts to determine if this is an actual temporal anomaly or psychological manipulation by a contained entity, and the researcher's struggle to trust their own perception. First person (researcher's perspective with interspersed notes), past tense. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**SCP-XXXX: "Temporal Notes"** I'm writing this report in a state of utter confusion and fear. It started about three weeks ago, when I found a handwritten note on my desk with my own handwriting. It was a simple message: "Don't let it happen. They're not what they seem." I thought it was just a prank from one of my colleagues, but as I read on, I realized that the note was talking about a containment breach that hadn't happened yet. At first, I dismissed it as a joke or a mistake, but as the days went by, more notes appeared. They were always on my desk, always with my handwriting, and always warning about the same breach. The notes became increasingly desperate and incoherent, sometimes containing information that contradicted known reality. **Note 1:** "Containment breach imminent. Don't trust Dr. Kim. He's been compromised." I showed the note to Dr. Kim, and he just laughed it off, saying it was probably a prank from one of the new interns. But I couldn't shake off the feeling that something was off. **Note 2:** "They're watching us. They're waiting for the perfect moment to strike. Don't go to the cafeteria on Thursday." I tried to ignore the note, but on Thursday, I found myself avoiding the cafeteria. I told myself it was just paranoia, but the feeling of being watched lingered. As the notes continued to appear, I started to feel like I was losing my grip on reality. I couldn't trust my own perception anymore. Was I really seeing these notes, or was it all just a product of my own paranoia? **Note 3:** "The breach will happen on March 15th. Don't try to stop it. You'll only make it worse." I reported the note to my superiors, and they launched an investigation into possible temporal anomalies. But as they dug deeper, they found nothing. No evidence of any kind of time travel or manipulation. It was as if the notes were just a product of my own imagination. But I knew what I saw. I knew what I felt. **Note 4:** "I'm trying to warn you. I'm trying to change the course of events. But it's too late. The breach has already happened. You're just a pawn in their game." The notes started to contradict each other, and I began to question my own sanity. Was I really communicating with my future self, or was I just being manipulated by some kind of entity? The Foundation brought in a team of psychologists to evaluate my mental state, but they found nothing out of the ordinary. I was deemed fit for duty, but I knew that something was wrong. **Note 5:** "I'm not who you think I am. I'm not even human. I'm just a vessel for something greater. Don't trust anything." I started to feel like I was trapped in some kind of never-ending nightmare. I couldn't trust my own thoughts, my own perceptions. I was just a pawn in a game I didn't understand. The Foundation launched a full-scale investigation into possible psychological manipulation by a contained entity. They scoured the records, looking for any sign of a breach or a anomaly. But they found nothing. **Note 6:** "It's too late. The breach has happened. The world is ending. You're just a footnote in history." I'm writing this report now, and I'm not sure what's real and what's not. I'm not sure if I'm really seeing these notes or if it's all just a product of my own mind. But I know one thing - I'm scared. I'm scared of what's coming, and I'm scared of what I might become. **Addendum:** The security cameras in the researcher's office have been found to glitch exactly at the moment new notes appear on the desk. The cause of this glitch is currently unknown. **Incident Report:** On//20, the researcher reported a containment breach in the cafeteria. The breach was later confirmed, and the entity responsible was found to be a previously unknown anomaly. The researcher's notes had predicted the breach, but the details were inconsistent with the actual events. The researcher is currently undergoing psychological evaluation and is being held in a secure facility for further observation. **Conclusion:** SCP-XXXX is currently classified as a possible temporal anomaly or psychological manipulation by a contained entity. Further research is needed to determine the true nature of the phenomenon.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to fulfill the SCP format requirements while telling a first-person narrative about temporal anomalies, but it suffers from several significant weaknesses that undermine its effectiveness. The adherence to instructions is mixed. While the piece does present a researcher finding notes from their future self and includes Foundation investigation elements, it fails to maintain consistent first-person perspective throughout, awkwardly switching between personal narrative and clinical SCP documentation. The 1000-word target is roughly met, but the execution feels rushed and underdeveloped. The character work is particularly weak. The unnamed researcher lacks distinct personality traits, motivations, or believable psychological responses to increasingly bizarre circumstances. Their descent into confusion and paranoia feels mechanical rather than organic, with emotional states simply stated rather than demonstrated through behavior or internal monologue. The supporting characters like Dr. Kim are mere names without substance. The writing style is inconsistent, jumping between informal first-person narration and clinical SCP documentation without smooth transitions. The voice lacks the professional detachment typically expected in SCP writing, while also failing to provide compelling personal insight from the researcher's perspective. The notes themselves, which should be the centerpiece of the anomaly, are disappointingly generic and lack the specific, unsettling details that would make them memorable. They read more like placeholder text than carefully crafted elements of psychological horror. The piece relies heavily on telling rather than showing, particularly in describing the researcher's emotional state and the Foundation's investigation. Critical plot points like the actual containment breach are mentioned in passing without proper development or impact. The ending feels abrupt and unearned, with the researcher's fate resolved through exposition rather than dramatic conclusion. The ambiguity about whether the phenomenon is real or psychological manipulation is handled clumsily, leaving readers unsatisfied rather than intriguingly uncertain. Technical issues include awkward phrasing, repetitive sentence structures, and formatting inconsistencies that detract from immersion. The piece lacks the clinical precision that makes effective SCP writing compelling while also failing to provide the emotional depth needed for engaging first-person horror. + Scp: Unmarked Doors Archive — Score: 48.8
Prompt:
Write an SCP entry about a series of identical unmarked doors appearing in abandoned buildings worldwide that lead to a massive, architecturally impossible archive. Documents within reference a previous global civilization destroyed by an unspecified containment failure. Foundation researchers discover references to their own organization under a different name, including personnel files for current staff dated centuries ago. Include exploration logs revealing sections of the archive actively being removed by entities resembling hazmat teams who flee when approached, and evidence that O5 Council members have visited the archive without authorization. Third person (exploration team perspective) with recovered document excerpts. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**SCP-XXXX: "The Archive of Elyria"** **Object Class:** Euclid **Special Containment Procedures:** All instances of SCP-XXXX are to be monitored and secured by Foundation personnel. Access to the archive is restricted to Level 3 personnel and above, with all exploration and research activities requiring prior approval from at least two Level 4 personnel. The O5 Council has been notified of the potential breach of protocol and is currently investigating the unauthorized visits. **Description:** SCP-XXXX refers to a series of identical, unmarked doors that have appeared in abandoned buildings worldwide. These doors, measuring 2.5 meters in height and 1.5 meters in width, are made of a smooth, gray material that does not appear to be any known metal or alloy. The doors are always found in areas with no visible means of entry or exit, and their appearance is often accompanied by a faint, pulsating glow emanating from the edges. When opened, each door leads to a massive, architecturally impossible archive. The interior of the archive is a labyrinthine network of shelves, corridors, and reading rooms, stretching for kilometers in every direction. The walls, floor, and ceiling are made of a gleaming white material that seems almost liquid in appearance. The air is stale and musty, with a faint scent of old paper and dust. The archive contains an vast array of documents, including books, scrolls, and digital storage devices. These documents are written in a variety of languages, including some that are no longer spoken. Many of the documents reference a previous global civilization, known as "Elyria," which was destroyed by an unspecified containment failure. The documents also mention a organization known as "The Keepers," which bears a striking resemblance to the Foundation. **Recovery Log:** On//20, a team of Foundation researchers, led by Dr., entered the archive through an instance of SCP-XXXX in an abandoned warehouse in [REDACTED]. The team consisted of Dr., a historian; Dr., an expert in ancient languages; and Agent, a security specialist. As they explored the archive, the team stumbled upon a section dedicated to "The Keepers." The documents within this section included personnel files for current Foundation staff, dated centuries ago. The team also found references to the O5 Council, including minutes from meetings that took place over 500 years ago. **Document Excerpt 1:** "...The Keepers, in their infinite wisdom, have decreed that the containment of [REDACTED] is of utmost importance. All resources will be allocated to ensure the continued security of this anomaly. Signed, [REDACTED], Keeper of the Seventh Circle." **Document Excerpt 2:** "...The Elyrian Incident has resulted in catastrophic consequences. The breach of [REDACTED] has unleashed a horror beyond comprehension. The Keepers are left to pick up the pieces and rebuild. Signed, [REDACTED], Keeper of the First Circle." As the team delved deeper into the archive, they encountered sections that appeared to be actively being removed by entities resembling hazmat teams. These entities, clad in black suits and masks, would flee when approached, leaving behind scattered documents and debris. **Exploration Log 2:** On//20, the team encountered a group of entities removing documents from a section dedicated to "Anomalous Entities." The entities, when approached, dropped their equipment and fled through a door that appeared to lead to a non-existent corridor. The team recovered several documents, including one that referenced an anomaly known as "The Devourer of Worlds." **Document Excerpt 3:** "...The Devourer of Worlds, a creature of unmitigated horror, has been contained by The Keepers. Its power is beyond human comprehension, and its very existence threatens the fabric of reality. Signed, [REDACTED], Keeper of the Ninth Circle." Further exploration revealed evidence that O5 Council members had visited the archive without authorization. The team found a hidden logbook, belonging to an unknown O5 member, detailing their visits to the archive over the past decade. **Logbook Excerpt:** "...I have returned to the archive, and I am convinced that The Keepers are not just a historical organization. They are a warning, a message from the past. We must learn from their mistakes and ensure that we do not repeat them. The fate of humanity depends on it. Signed, [REDACTED], O5-" The implications of SCP-XXXX are profound, and the Foundation is left to wonder about the true nature of its own existence. Is the Foundation a continuation of The Keepers, or is it a new organization, doomed to repeat the mistakes of the past? The answer, much like the contents of the archive, remains a mystery, waiting to be uncovered. **Addendum:** Following the discovery of the unauthorized visits by O5 Council members, the O5 Council has issued a statement assuring the Foundation that an investigation is underway. The statement reads: "The O5 Council takes the allegations of unauthorized visits to SCP-XXXX seriously and is currently investigating the matter. We assure the Foundation that we will take all necessary steps to ensure the integrity of our organization and the safety of our personnel."

[Analysis] This SCP entry demonstrates a solid understanding of the Foundation universe's format and tone, successfully incorporating the requested elements including the mysterious doors, impossible archive, references to a predecessor civilization called "The Keepers," and unauthorized O5 Council visits. However, the execution lacks the subtle horror and meticulous detail that characterize the best SCP entries. + Classic sci-fi: Offworlder (Le Guin) — Score: 61.8
Prompt:
Classic sci-fi: Offworlder (Author style: Le Guin) Write a chapter following a young diplomatic envoy sent to address tensions on a distant human colony where humanity has diverged into distinct subspecies through both natural adaptation and separation of lineages. Against protocol, the envoy slips away from official functions to walk the streets alone, encountering markets, ordinary citizens, and social structures that contradict the official briefings. Upon returning to their quarters, the envoy is reprimanded by Command, and is tasked with approaching the stationed Minister of Science (a political posting rather than scientific). A challenging conversation ensues, in which the envoy's wits and will are tested, by a seasoned political operator looking to test the mettle of the offworlder. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
Chapter 7: The Unseen Streets As the sun set on the dusty colony town, casting a warm orange glow over the makeshift market stalls, Aria slipped away from the official delegation. She had been warned not to venture out alone, not to stray from the carefully planned itinerary, but the stifling protocol and rehearsed smiles had become too much to bear. The urge to experience the true pulse of the colony, to see beyond the curated façade, had grown too strong to resist. Aria navigated the winding alleys, her eyes drinking in the vibrant colors and eclectic sounds of the market. The air was thick with the scent of exotic spices, fresh bread, and the sweet tang of ripening fruit. She marveled at the handwoven fabrics on display, the intricate patterns and hues unlike anything she had seen before. A stall owner, noticing her interest, beckoned her closer, offering a sample of the finest silk-like material, dyed in a pigment that shimmered like the stars on a clear night. "From the depths of our own soil," the vendor said with a warm smile, "the essence of the terra itself, infused into every thread." Aria's fingers caressed the fabric, feeling the subtle texture and weight. She had been briefed on the colony's unique properties, the way the native soil and microorganisms had adapted to the alien environment, but to see it manifested in such beauty was a revelation. As she continued her stroll, Aria encountered a group of children playing in the street, their laughter and shouts mingling with the calls of vendors and the hum of the market. They were a mix of phenotypes, some with skin that shimmered like the moon, others with eyes that seemed to see right through her. She watched, entranced, as they chased each other, their joy and energy infectious. But not everyone shared their exuberance. Aria noticed a group of individuals, standing apart from the crowd, their features more angular, their skin a deep, burnished copper. They eyed her warily, their gaze like a challenge. She felt a shiver run down her spine as she realized that these must be the Kaelin, the subspecies that had developed in the harsh, arid regions of the colony. The briefings had warned of their isolationism and suspicion towards outsiders. Aria's wanderings eventually led her back to the diplomatic quarters, where she was greeted by a stern-faced aide. "Envoy, you were expected at the reception two hours ago. Command is... displeased." Aria's heart sank as she followed the aide to the comms room, where a holographic projection of Command's face glared at her. "Envoy Aria, your actions are unacceptable. You were explicitly instructed to adhere to the itinerary. Your... curiosity... puts the entire mission at risk." Aria stood tall, her voice steady. "I apologize, Command. I needed to understand the colony beyond the official briefings. I assure you, my actions were not reckless." Command's expression did not soften. "You will meet with Minister Elwes, our liaison with the Science Ministry. She will... enlighten you on the true nature of this colony and its people." Aria was ushered into the Minister's office, a sleek, modern space that seemed out of place in the rustic colony town. Minister Elwes, a woman with a sharp jawline and piercing green eyes, rose from behind her desk, her smile a calculated gesture. "Envoy Aria, delighted to finally meet you. I trust you're finding our humble colony... enlightening?" Aria's instincts warned her that this was a woman not to be underestimated. "Minister Elwes, I'm grateful for the opportunity to discuss the colony's... complexities. The market, the people, the—" Elwes's laughter cut her off, a low, husky sound. "Ah, the market. Yes, we have... colorful traditions here. But let's not be distracted by the superficial. You see, Envoy, this colony is a delicate ecosystem, with many... competing interests. The Kaelin, for example, are not as... welcoming as the others. They have their own agenda, one that may not align with our... mutual goals." Aria's eyes locked onto the Minister's, her mind racing. "I understand that the Kaelin have developed in isolation, but surely, we can find common ground?" Elwes's smile grew wider, her eyes glinting with amusement. "Oh, Envoy, you are so... naive. The Kaelin are not just a subspecies, they're a symbol of resistance. A reminder that not everyone shares our... vision for this colony's future. You see, we have... investments to protect, interests to serve. And sometimes, that means making difficult choices." Aria's will hardened, her voice firm. "I understand the complexities, Minister, but as a representative of the Union, I must prioritize the well-being of all citizens, regardless of subspecies or affiliation. I will not be swayed by... competing interests." Elwes's expression turned icy, her voice dripping with condescension. "Ah, Envoy, you really are... refreshing. I almost believe you think you can make a difference. But let me tell you, in this game, the players are not always what they seem. And the stakes are far higher than you can imagine." The Minister's words hung in the air, a challenge, a warning, and a test. Aria met her gaze, unwavering, her mind racing with the implications of what she had just heard. She knew that she had to tread carefully, to navigate the treacherous waters of the colony's politics, but she was determined to uncover the truth, no matter the cost.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece attempts to capture Le Guin's style and fulfill the prompt's requirements, with mixed success. The author establishes the basic scenario competently - a diplomatic envoy exploring beyond official boundaries and facing political consequences. The worldbuilding shows effort, introducing subspecies like the Kaelin and incorporating environmental adaptation themes that echo Le Guin's anthropological interests. However, the execution falls short of Le Guin's sophisticated approach in several key areas. The prose lacks her characteristic restraint and philosophical depth, occasionally veering toward purple prose with phrases like "essence of the terra itself, infused into every thread." The dialogue, particularly with Minister Elwes, feels somewhat stilted and overly expository, with the Minister's repeated use of ellipses creating an artificial speech pattern that undermines naturalism. The character development shows promise but remains surface-level. Aria's motivations are clear but not deeply explored, and her transformation from curious envoy to determined truth-seeker feels somewhat rushed. Minister Elwes comes across as a fairly standard political antagonist without the complexity Le Guin would typically bring to such figures. The worldbuilding elements work adequately - the market scene provides sensory detail and the subspecies concept aligns with the prompt. However, the social tensions feel underdeveloped, and the political dynamics lack the nuanced ambiguity characteristic of Le Guin's work. Structurally, the piece follows the prompt's requirements but feels episodic rather than organically flowing. The transition from market exploration to political confrontation works functionally but lacks emotional resonance. The ending sets up future conflict appropriately but doesn't provide meaningful resolution or insight. The writing demonstrates competence in basic storytelling mechanics but lacks the literary sophistication and philosophical depth that would truly capture Le Guin's voice and approach to science fiction. + Biopunk: Polymerase Chain Reaction — Score: 63.0
Prompt:
Biopunk -- Polymerase Chain Reaction Write a chapter set in a near-future post-apocalyptic world where corporate genetic engineering was designed with built-in obsolescence—engineered DNA lasting only one generation to maximize profits before societal collapse. Follow a biohacker working with salvaged equipment to splice viable food crops for their settlement using rapidly degrading genetic material. As world building / window dressing, include details about jury-rigged lab equipment, and the physical toll (and unexpected upsides) of using untested genetic modifications as medicine. The plot of this chapter is centred around a black market contract. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
Chapter 7: The Splicer's Dilemma The air was thick with the smell of ozone and burned plastic as I hunched over the makeshift lab bench. Flickering LEDs cast eerie shadows on the walls, illuminating the sprawl of scavenged equipment. My eyes watered from the fumes of the jury-rigged PCR machine, cobbled together from scraps of pre-Collapse technology. The glow-in-the-dark mushrooms sprouting from the cracked tiles seemed to pulse with an otherworldly energy, a reminder of the unpredictable nature of my work. I was a biohacker, one of the few who still dared to tinker with the genetic code in a world where corporate-engineered DNA was designed to self-destruct. The megacorps had built in obsolescence, creating a never-ending cycle of consumption and profit. But when the world collapsed, their carefully crafted genetic time bombs detonated, leaving behind a legacy of decay and degradation. My settlement, New Eden, was a ragtag community of survivors who'd banded together to rebuild. We needed sustainable food sources, and that's where I came in. I'd been contracted by the settlement's leader, a grizzled old soldier named Marcus, to create a strain of hardy, disease-resistant crops using whatever genetic material I could scrounge up. The problem was, the DNA I worked with was rapidly degrading. The corporations had built in a "kill switch" to ensure their products wouldn't be viable beyond a single generation. It was a ticking time bomb, and I was racing against the clock to create something that would last. I carefully pipetted a sample of the latest batch of genetic material into the PCR machine. The device whirred to life, its makeshift casing rattling ominously as it amplified the DNA. I watched the readout, my heart sinking as the error rate climbed. This batch was worse than the last. The genetic material was breaking down faster than I could work with it. Just then, a knock at the door interrupted my concentration. It was a hooded figure, dressed in tattered streetwear. "Splicer," they said, their voice distorted by a voice modulator. "I have a job for you." I eyed them warily, but the promise of payment was too enticing to resist. "What do you need?" "A custom splice," they replied, producing a data pad with a cryptic set of specifications. "I want a strain of wheat that's resistant to the Newhaven virus. And I need it fast." I raised an eyebrow. The Newhaven virus was a particularly nasty strain that had devastated crops worldwide. Creating a resistant strain would be a challenge, but the payoff could be huge. "What's the payment?" The figure hesitated before producing a small pouch of synthetic insulin. "This is the good stuff, Splicer. Enough to keep you and your people going for a while." My eyes widened. Synthetic insulin was a luxury in our world, and this pouch was worth a small fortune. But at what cost? The black market was notorious for its untested, unpredictable genetic modifications. Using this insulin as medicine could have unforeseen consequences. I weighed my options. The settlement needed food, and this contract could provide the resources to make that happen. But if I failed, or if the genetic material proved too unstable...the risks were too great to ignore. "I'll take the job," I said finally, tucking the pouch into my pocket. "But I need a guarantee: if this splice goes sideways, you'll provide us with a safe haven. We can't afford to be caught in the crossfire." The figure nodded, its hood bobbing in agreement. "You have my word, Splicer. Just get it done." As the figure disappeared into the night, I felt a thrill of excitement mixed with trepidation. This contract could be the key to New Eden's survival, or its downfall. I set to work, pouring all my knowledge and skill into the splice. The hours blurred together as I worked, the glow-in-the-dark mushrooms watching over me like sentinels. The PCR machine hummed along, spitting out fragments of DNA that I carefully assembled into a coherent whole. Finally, after what felt like an eternity, I had a viable sample. I injected it into a test subject – a hapless wheat sprout – and waited. The results were nothing short of miraculous. The wheat grew strong and healthy, resisting the Newhaven virus with ease. I felt a surge of pride and accomplishment, knowing that this could be the breakthrough New Eden needed. But as I gazed at the thriving wheat, I couldn't shake the feeling that I'd just made a deal with a devil. The black market insulin was still clutched in my pocket, a reminder of the risks I'd taken. What unforeseen consequences would this contract bring? Only time would tell.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This biopunk chapter demonstrates a solid understanding of the genre requirements and prompt specifications. The author successfully establishes a post-apocalyptic world where corporate genetic engineering with built-in obsolescence has led to societal collapse, and follows a biohacker working with degrading genetic material to create viable crops. The worldbuilding elements are well-integrated, featuring jury-rigged lab equipment like a makeshift PCR machine "cobbled together from scraps" and atmospheric details such as glow-in-the-dark mushrooms growing from cracked tiles. The central premise of DNA designed to self-destruct after one generation is compelling and well-executed throughout the narrative. The black market contract plot unfolds naturally, with a mysterious hooded figure offering synthetic insulin in exchange for creating virus-resistant wheat. The protagonist's internal conflict between the settlement's needs and the risks involved creates appropriate tension. However, the piece suffers from several notable weaknesses. The dialogue feels stilted and functional rather than natural, particularly the exchanges with the hooded figure which rely on generic thriller tropes. The character development is shallow - the protagonist remains largely undefined beyond their role as "the biohacker," lacking distinctive personality traits or compelling personal stakes. The prose occasionally veers toward purple territory with phrases like "otherworldly energy" and "sentinels," though it generally maintains readability. The pacing is somewhat rushed, particularly in the resolution where the successful splice happens too quickly and easily, undermining the established difficulty of working with degrading genetic material. The ending feels somewhat unearned in its success, given the emphasis on how challenging and unstable the genetic material is supposed to be. The protagonist's moral concerns about the black market deal are introduced but not deeply explored, missing an opportunity for greater emotional complexity. The technical aspects of the biopunk elements are handled competently, though they could be more deeply integrated into the character's experience. The physical toll of genetic modifications is mentioned but not fully developed as promised in the prompt.
